## 医(醫)院
---
## hospital
### yīyuàn
---
- **traditional:** 醫院
- **definition:** hospital
- **pinyin:** yīyuàn
- **components:**
  - 医(醫)
    - yī
    - medicine; doctor
  - 院
    - yuàn
    - courtyard; institution
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:**
    - 医(醫) (yī, "medicine; doctor") + 院 (yuàn, "courtyard; institution") =
    - an institution for practicing medicine ->
    - hospital
  - **interpretation:** A 院 (yuàn, "institution") where 医(醫) (yī, "medicine") is practiced is a place where people go to receive medical treatment and healthcare.
- **examples:**
  - 我去医(醫)院，看医(醫)生。
    - Wǒ qù yīyuàn, kàn yīshēng.
    - I go to the hospital to see a doctor.
  - 医(醫)院在城市中心，设(設)备(備)先进(進)。
    - Yīyuàn zài chéngshì zhōngxīn, shèbèi xiānjìn.
    - The hospital is located in the city center with advanced equipment.
  - 医(醫)生在医(醫)院救治病人。
    - Yīshēng zài yīyuàn jiùzhì bìngrén.
    - Doctors treat patients in the hospital.
### 医(醫)院 → 医(醫)
- **traditional:** 醫
- **definition:** medicine; doctor
- **pinyin:** yī
- **components:**
  - 匸
    - xì
    - that which hides; that which stores
  - 矢
    - shǐ
    - arrow

  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 匸 (that which hides) + 矢 (arrow) =
    - a hidden arrow ->
    - metaphor for treating (hidden dangers addressed by medicine)
  - **interpretation:** The character combines the concepts of 'hide' with 'arrow', suggesting the idea of dealing with hidden threats or illnesses, akin to specialized knowledge required for healing.

- **definition:** arrow

  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an arrow
  - **interpretation:** The character 矢(shǐ, 'arrow') is a pictogram representing an arrow. Its resemblance to arrows was more evident in ancient script forms.

### 医(醫)院 → 院
- **definition:** courtyard; institution
- **pinyin:** yuàn
- **components:**
  - 阝
    - fù
    - hill; mound
  - 完
    - wán
    - complete
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 阝 (fù, "hill; mound") + phonetic 完 (wán, "complete") ->
    - courtyard
  - **interpretation:** The character 院(yuàn, "courtyard; institution") is formed by the semantic component 阝 (fù, "hill; mound"), suggesting an enclosed or defined space, combined with the phonetic component 完 (wán, "complete"), contributing the sound. The idea of a 'courtyard' as a defined, enclosed space aligns with the semantic implication of 阝. In extended use, the character refers to institutions, which are also defined spaces pertaining to specific functions.
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)在医(醫)院对(對)面吃饭(飯)。
    - Wǒmen zài yīyuàn duìmiàn chīfàn.
    - We are eating opposite the hospital.
  - 学(學)校的院子里(裡)有很多花。
    - Xuéxiào de yuànzi lǐ yǒu hěn duō huā.
    - There are many flowers in the school's courtyard.
  - 这(這)家研究院专(專)注于(於)环(環)保技术(術)。
    - Zhè jiā yánjiūyuàn zhuānzhù yú huánbǎo jìshù.
    - This research institute focuses on environmental technology.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 院](@media/glyph9662.png)
### 医(醫)院 → 院 → 阝
- **definition:** hill; mound
- **pinyin:** fù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a small mound or hillock.
  - **interpretation:** The character 阝 (fù, 'mound') visually represents a small elevation of land, resembling a hillside or embankment.
- **examples:**
  - 小山顶(頂)上耸(聳)立着(著)阝(阜)。
    - Xiǎo shāndǐng shàng sǒnglì zhe fù.
    - A small mound stands atop the hill.
  - 山坡上长(長)满(滿)了绿(綠)色的草丛(叢)，山丘边(邊)坐落着(著)一座古老的阝(阜)。
    - Shānpō shàng cháng mǎn le lǜsè de cǎocóng, shānqiū biān zuòluò zhe yī zuò gǔlǎo de fù.
    - The hillside is covered with green grass, and an ancient mound sits by the hill.
  - 远(遠)处(處)沙丘边(邊)隐(隱)约(約)可见(見)一堆阝(阜)，仿(彷)佛(彿)历(歷)史的见(見)证(證)。
    - Yuǎnchù shāqiū biān yǐnyuē kějiàn yī duī fù, fǎngfú lìshǐ de jiànzhèng.
    - In the distance, a pile of mounds is barely visible by the sand dunes, as if witnessing history.
### 医(醫)院 → 院 → 完
- **definition:** complete
- **pinyin:** wán
- **components:**
  - 宀
    - mián
    - roof
  - 元
    - yuán
    - origin
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 宀 (roof) + phonetic 元 (sound) ->
    - finished; intact
  - **interpretation:** The character 完 (wán, "finished; intact") combines the semantic element 宀 (mián, "roof"), suggesting a protective or structural component, and the phonetic element 元 (yuán, "origin"), indicating the pronunciation. Together, they imply a structure that is completed and covered, hence the sense of something being "finished" or "intact."
- **examples:**
  - 他终(終)于(於)完成任务(務)了。
    - Tā zhōngyú wánchéng rènwù le.
    - He finally finished the task.
  - 晚餐做好了，可以开(開)饭(飯)了。
    - Wǎncān zuò hǎo le, kěyǐ kāifàn le.
    - Dinner is finished and ready to be served.
  - 我的工作还(還)没(沒)完，需要加班。
    - Wǒ de gōngzuò hái méi wán, xūyào jiābān.
    - My work is not finished yet and I need to work overtime.
### 医(醫)院 → 院 → 完 → 宀
- **definition:** roof
- **pinyin:** mián
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a house with four walls ->
    - roof
  - **interpretation:** 宀(mián, "roof") is a pictogram representing a house with four walls. It emphasizes an enclosed space, distinguishing it from similar structures like 广(guǎng, "broad") which depicts a building with three walls. This makes 宀 a logical choice for representing a roof in various characters.
- **examples:**
  - 含有宀的汉(漢)字代表家的温(溫)暖。
    - Hán yǒu mián de hànzì dàibiǎo jiā de wēnnuǎn.
    - Chinese characters that include the radical '宀' represent the warmth of home.
  - 屋顶(頂)遮风(風)挡(擋)雨，家园(園)散发(發)温(溫)馨。
    - Wūdǐng zhē fēng dǎng yǔ, jiāyuán sànfā wēnxīn.
    - The roof shields from wind and rain, and the home radiates warmth.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 宀](@media/glyph5b80.png)
### 医(醫)院 → 院 → 完 → 元
- **definition:** origin
- **pinyin:** yuán
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a human head above a horizontal line, symbolizing the origin or the head of something
  - **interpretation:** 元 (yuán, 'origin') represents the head, which is often considered the starting point or leader, aligning with the concept of 'origin'. This setup also connects metaphorically to beginnings or first principles.
- **examples:**
  - 万(萬)物之元来(來)自于(於)混沌。
    - Wànwù zhī yuán láizì yú húndùn.
    - The origin of all things comes from chaos.
  - 道家的理念追寻(尋)心灵(靈)的元。
    - Dàojiā de lǐniàn zhuīxún xīnlíng de yuán.
    - Taoist philosophy seeks the origin of the soul.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 元](@media/glyph5143.png)

## 需要

## to need
### xūyào
---
- **definition:** to need
- **pinyin:** xūyào
- **components:**
  - 需
    - xū
    - to need; to require; to have to
  - 要
    - yào
    - to want; to demand; essential; important
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:**
    - 需 (xū, "to need; to require; to have to") + 要 (yào, "to want; to demand; essential; important") =
    - a situation or thing that is both needed and wanted
  - **interpretation:** 需 (xū, "to need; to require") involves the idea of necessity, something you must have or do. 要 (yào, "to want; to demand") emphasizes desire or importance. Combining these, 需要(xūyào) indicates something that is both necessary and desired, hence 'to need'.
- **examples:**
  - 我需要你的帮(幫)助。
    - Wǒ xūyào nǐ de bāngzhù.
    - I need your help.
  - 如果你需要休息，就告诉(訴)我。
    - Rúguǒ nǐ xūyào xiūxī, jiù gàosù wǒ.
    - If you need a rest, just tell me.
  - 她需要更多的时(時)间(間)来(來)完成工作。
    - Tā xūyào gèng duō de shíjiān lái wánchéng gōngzuò.
    - She needs more time to complete the work.
### 需要 → 需
- **definition:** to need; to require; to have to
- **pinyin:** xū
- **components:**
  - 天
    - tiān
    - person
  - 雨
    - yǔ
    - rain
  - 而
    - ér
    - then
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 天 (tiān, "person") + 雨 (yǔ, "rain") =
    - person getting wet in the rain ->
    - 天 corrupted to 而 (ér) ->
    - final form is 需
  - **interpretation:** The character 需 originally depicted a person getting wet in the rain, showing a need or requirement to stay dry. Over time, 天 (tiān, "person") was replaced by a corrupted form 而 (ér) during the Han dynasty, leading to the modern character.
- **examples:**
  - 学(學)生需努力学(學)习(習)。
    - Xuéshēng xū nǔlì xuéxí.
    - Students must study diligently.
  - 工程师(師)需解决(決)问(問)题(題)，团(團)队(隊)需协(協)同合作。
    - Gōngchéngshī xū jiějué wèntí, tuánduì xū xiétóng hézuò.
    - Engineers need to solve problems, and the team needs to cooperate.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 需](@media/glyph9700.png)
### 需要 → 需 → 天
- **definition:** person
- **pinyin:** tiān
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Horizontal line above 大(dà, "big") to depict sky ->
    - anthropomorphic man with large head symbolizing heaven
  - **interpretation:** The character 天(tiān) originally depicts the sky as a horizontal line above a person with outstretched arms, 大(dà, "big"), emphasizing the vastness or domain of heaven. Over time, the character evolved into an anthropomorphic representation of heaven, which later influenced its interpretation in classical texts.
- **examples:**
  - 夜幕降临(臨)，天边(邊)星光闪(閃)烁(爍)。
    - Yèmù jiànglín, tiānbiān xīnguāng shǎnshuò.
    - As night falls, starlight gleams on the horizon.
  - 他仰望高空，祈求天佑众(眾)生。
    - Tā yǎngwàng gāokōng, qíqiú tiānyòu zhòngshēng.
    - He gazes up to the sky and prays for heaven's protection over all living beings.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 天](@media/glyph5929.png)
### 需要 → 需 → 雨
- **definition:** rain
- **pinyin:** yǔ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a cloud with drops of rain falling from it ->
    - horizontal stroke added later ->
    - rain
  - **interpretation:** 雨 (yǔ, "rain") visually represents rain falling from a cloud, capturing its essential form.
- **examples:**
  - 今天雨下得很大。
    - Jīntiān yǔ xià de hěn dà.
    - It rained hard today.
  - 他忘记(記)带(帶)伞(傘)，雨却(卻)毫不留情。
    - Tā wàngjì dài sǎn, yǔ què háobù liúqíng.
    - He forgot to bring an umbrella, and the rain showed no mercy.
  - 细(細)雨如丝(絲)，轻(輕)拂着(著)花瓣。
    - Xì yǔ rú sī, qīng fú zhe huā bàn.
    - The fine rain falls like silk, gently brushing the petals.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 雨](@media/glyph96e8.png)
### 需要 → 需 → 而
- **definition:** then
- **pinyin:** ér
- **components:**
  - 耏
    - ér
    - beard
  - 髵
    - ér
    - beard
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a beard ->
    - original form of 耏 or 髵
  - **interpretation:** The character 而 initially depicted a beard, which shares visual similarities to the concept of 'and then' due to the flow and continuity implied by hair, thus connecting to transitional ideas.
- **examples:**
  - 他努力工作，而他的老板(闆)却(卻)不满(滿)意他的表现(現)。
    - Tā nǔlì gōngzuò, ér tā de lǎobǎn què bù mǎnyì tā de biǎoxiàn.
    - He works hard, yet his boss is not satisfied with his performance.
  - 我很想去旅行，而这(這)次疫情使我无(無)法成行。
    - Wǒ hěn xiǎng qù lǚxíng, ér zhè cì yìqíng shǐ wǒ wúfǎ chéng xíng.
    - I really want to travel, but the pandemic has made it impossible for me.
  - 猫(貓)抓住了小鸟(鳥)，而它却(卻)没(沒)有伤(傷)害它。
    - Māo zhuā zhù le xiǎo niǎo, ér tā què méiyǒu shānghài tā.
    - The cat caught the bird, but it did not harm it.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 而](@media/glyph800c.png)
### 需要 → 需 → 而 → 耏
- **definition:** beard
- **pinyin:** ér
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts the head of a person with a stylized beard ->
    - original meaning: beard
  - **interpretation:** The character 耏 (něi) originally depicted the head of a person with a stylized representation of a beard, directly reflecting its meaning related to 'beard'. The pictogram visually conveys the image of facial hair.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 耏](@media/glyph800f.png)
### 需要 → 需 → 而 → 髵
- **definition:** beard
- **pinyin:** ér
- **components:**
  - 髟
    - biāo
    - long hair
  - 兒
    - ér
    - child
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 髟 (biāo, "long hair") + phonetic 兒 (ér) ->
    - hair, beard
  - **interpretation:** The character 髵 combines the semantic 髟 (biāo, "long hair"), which conveys the connection to hair or beard, with the phonetic element 兒 (ér), which provides the sound. The combination effectively describes hair or beard, both recurring concepts linked to long hair.
### 需要 → 需 → 而 → 髵 → 髟
- **definition:** long hair
- **pinyin:** biāo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a person with long hair ->
    - represents long hair
  - **interpretation:** The character 髟(biāo, "hair") is a pictogram, symbolizing a person adorned with long hair, emphasizing its characteristic texture and appearance.
- **examples:**
  - 她的髟柔顺(順)如丝(絲)。
    - Tā de biāo róushùn rú sī.
    - Her hair is as smooth as silk.
  - 他每天早上花时(時)间(間)整理髟，保持整洁(潔)。
    - Tā měitiān zǎoshang huā shíjiān zhěnglǐ biāo, bǎochí zhěngjié.
    - He spends time every morning tidying his hair, keeping it neat.
  - 这(這)本字典详(詳)细(細)介绍(紹)了髟的历(歷)史。
    - Zhè běn zìdiǎn xiángxì jièshào le biāo de lìshǐ.
    - This dictionary details the history of the hair radical.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 髟](@media/glyph9adf.png)
### 需要 → 需 → 而 → 髵 → 兒
- **definition:** child
- **pinyin:** ér
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts an infant with an imperfect cranium ->
    - represents 'child'
  - **interpretation:** The pictogram captures the distinctive shape of a child's head, with the undeveloped cranium represented as open. This directly conveys the idea of a young child or infant.
- **examples:**
  - 那个(個)小孩在公园(園)里(裡)玩耍。
    - Nàge xiǎohái zài gōngyuán lǐ wánshuǎ.
    - The child is playing in the park.
  - 她的儿(兒)子聪(聰)明又好学(學)。
    - Tā de érzi cōngmíng yòu hàoxué.
    - Her child is smart and eager to learn.
  - 每个(個)家庭都希望他们(們)的孩子健康快乐(樂)。
    - Měi gè jiātíng dōu xīwàng tāmen de háizi jiànkāng kuàilè.
    - Every family hopes their children are healthy and happy.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 兒](@media/glyph5152.png)
### 需要 → 要
- **definition:** to want; to demand; essential; important
- **pinyin:** yào
- **components:**
  - 大
    - dà
    - large
  - 女
    - nǚ
    - woman
  - 目
    - mù
    - eye
  - 角
    - jiǎo
    - horn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 大 (large person) ->
    - 女 (woman) with hands pointing to midsection ->
    - 目 (eye) stylized as 角 (horn) ->
    - 覀 (stylized top) ->
    - final form 要 (yào, 'want; need; will; important')
  - **interpretation:** The character 要(yào, 'want; need; will; important') originally depicted a person with an eye on top, suggesting focus or necessity, which evolved through stylization into its current form. The hands indicating the midsection convey importance or centrality, aligning with meanings of ‘need’ and ‘want.’
- **examples:**
  - 我要喝水。
    - Wǒ yào hē shuǐ.
    - I want to drink water.
  - 如果你要成功，你就要努力学(學)习(習)。
    - Rúguǒ nǐ yào chénggōng, nǐ jiù yào nǔlì xuéxí.
    - If you want to succeed, you need to study hard.
  - 明天我要参(參)加会(會)议(議)，请(請)你不要迟(遲)到。
    - Míngtiān wǒ yào cānjiā huìyì, qǐng nǐ bùyào chídào.
    - I will attend the meeting tomorrow; please do not be late.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 要](@media/glyph8981.png)
### 需要 → 要 → 大
- **definition:** large
- **pinyin:** dà
- **components:**
  - 夫
    - fū
    - man
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a person facing forward ->
    - Borrowed phonetically for 'big'; original form of 夫 (fū, 'man')
  - **interpretation:** The character 大(dà) depicts a person facing forward, representing 'big' by suggesting the idea of someone standing prominently. Although often thought of as a person with outstretched arms, early scripts do not support this interpretation. It was originally the form of 夫 (fū, 'man') and was later phonetically borrowed for the meaning 'big.'
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)个(個)房子很大。
    - Zhè ge fángzi hěn dà.
    - This house is very big.
  - 大海波涛(濤)汹(洶)涌(湧)，展现(現)出大自然的力量。
    - Dàhǎi bōtāo xiōngyǒng, zhǎnxiàn chū dàzìrán de lìliàng.
    - The vast ocean waves surge, showcasing the power of nature.
  - 大人物登场(場)，留下传(傳)奇。
    - Dà rénwù dēngchǎng, liúxià chuánqí.
    - Great figures make an appearance, leaving behind legends.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 大](@media/glyph5927.png)
### 需要 → 要 → 大 → 夫
- **definition:** man
- **pinyin:** fū
- **components:**
  - 大
    - dà
    - big
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a variant form of 大 (dà, "big") representing an adult man with a hairpin ->
    - became associated with 夫 (fū, "man").
  - **interpretation:** 夫 (fū, "man") was visually similar to 大 (dà, "big") and was originally interchangeable. The addition of the horizontal stroke was interpreted as a hairpin, symbolizing adulthood for men.
- **examples:**
  - 此夫心怀(懷)大志。
    - Cǐ fū xīn huái dà zhì.
    - This man has lofty aspirations.
  - 他勤劳(勞)努力，堪称(稱)良夫。
    - Tā qín láo nǔ lì, kān chēng liáng fū.
    - He works diligently and is regarded as an exemplary man.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 夫](@media/glyph592b.png)
### 需要 → 要 → 女
- **definition:** woman
- **pinyin:** nǚ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a woman kneeling or standing ->
    - enclosed area as remnant of right breast
  - **interpretation:** The character 女(nǚ, "woman") is a pictogram originally depicting a woman with highlighted bodily features, such as the breasts, symbolizing femininity. Its orientation changed from the Oracle Bone script to face right, simplifying over time while still retaining the essence of its original depiction.
- **examples:**
  - 那位才华(華)横(橫)溢的女，赢(贏)得了全场(場)注目。
    - Nà wèi cáihuá héngyì de nǚ, yíng dé le quánchǎng zhùmù.
    - That talented woman won everyone's attention.
  - 古时(時)候‘女’常被用来(來)象征(徵)温(溫)柔，而如今它代表独(獨)立自信。
    - Gǔshíhòu ‘nǚ’ cháng bèi yòng lái xiàngzhēng wēnróu, ér rújīn tā dàibiǎo dúlì zìxìn.
    - In ancient times, the character '女' was often used to symbolize gentleness, whereas today it represents independence and confidence.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 女](@media/glyph5973.png)
### 需要 → 要 → 目
- **definition:** eye
- **pinyin:** mù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a human eye, now represented and rotated 90 degrees ->
    - eye
  - **interpretation:** The character 目(mù, 'eye') is a pictogram representing a human eye. Its original orientation has changed over time, resembling an eye seen from a sideways view.
- **examples:**
  - 他的目光炯炯有神。
    - Tā de mùguāng jiǒngjiǒng yǒu shén.
    - His gaze is bright and full of spirit.
  - 她目不转(轉)睛，注视(視)前方。
    - Tā mù bù zhuǎn jīng, zhùshì qiánfāng.
    - She stared intently, gazing ahead.
  - 雄鹰(鷹)展翅，双(雙)目炯炯看天际(際)。
    - Xióng yīng zhǎn chì, shuāng mù jiǒngjiǒng kàn tiānjì.
    - The eagle spreads its wings, its eyes piercingly gaze at the horizon.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 目](@media/glyph76ee.png)
### 需要 → 要 → 角
- **definition:** horn
- **pinyin:** jiǎo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an animal horn
  - **interpretation:** The character 角 (jiǎo, "horn") visually represents the distinctive shape of an animal's horn.
- **examples:**
  - 牛角是一种(種)坚(堅)固的天然武器。
    - niú jiǎo shì yī zhǒng jiān gù de tiān rán wǔ qì。
    - Cow horns are sturdy natural weapons.
  - 鹿角丰(豐)富了森林的传(傳)说(說)，象征(徵)着(著)自由与(與)力量。
    - lù jiǎo fēng fù le sēn lín de chuán shuō, xiàng zhēng zhe zì yóu yǔ lì liàng。
    - Deer antlers enrich the legends of the forest and symbolize freedom and strength.
  - 犀牛角在古代被视(視)作珍贵(貴)药(藥)材。
    - xī niú jiǎo zài gǔ dài bèi shì zuò zhēn guì yào cái。
    - Rhinoceros horns were regarded as precious medicinal materials in ancient times.

## 等
---
## to wait
### děng
---
- **definition:** to wait
- **pinyin:** děng
- **components:**
  - 竹
    - zhú
    - bamboo
  - 寺
    - sì
    - temple
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 竹 (zhú, "bamboo") + phonetic 寺 (sì, "temple") ->
    - bamboo strips for grading ->
    - rank; grade ->
    - borrowed for wait; await
  - **interpretation:** The bamboo strips, 竹 (zhú, "bamboo"), were used for writing and thus associated with record-keeping and classification leading to the meaning of rank or grade. The character 寺 (sì, "temple") contributes the phonetic sound. Over time, the character was borrowed to express 'wait' and 'await.'
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)在大门(門)口等你。
    - Wǒmen zài dàménkǒu děng nǐ.
    - We are waiting for you at the gate.
  - 请(請)等一下，我马(馬)上回来(來)！
    - Qǐng děng yīxià, wǒ mǎshàng huílái!
    - Please wait a moment, I will be back soon!
  - 他的学(學)术(術)水平很高，属(屬)于(於)一流的等级(級)。
    - Tā de xuéshù shuǐpíng hěn gāo, shǔyú yīliú de děngjí.
    - His academic level is very high, belonging to the top rank.
### 等 → 竹
- **definition:** bamboo
- **pinyin:** zhú
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts bamboo stalks with leaves
  - **interpretation:** The character 竹 (zhú, "bamboo") visually represents two stalks of bamboo with leaves at the top, illustrating the appearance of bamboo plants traditionally found in nature.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)根竹坚(堅)韧(韌)且美丽(麗)。
    - Zhè gēn zhú jiān rèn qiě měi lì.
    - This bamboo is strong and beautiful.
  - 竹子在风(風)中摇(搖)曳，发(發)出沙沙的声(聲)音。
    - Zhúzi zài fēng zhōng yáo yè, fā chū shā shā de shēng yīn.
    - The bamboo sways in the wind, making a rustling sound.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 竹](@media/glyph7af9.png)
### 等 → 寺
- **definition:** temple
- **pinyin:** sì
- **components:**
  - 𡳿
    - zhī
    - to go; footprint
  - 寸
    - cùn
    - inch
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 𡳿 ->
    - 之; 士 + semantic 又 (hand) ->
    - 寸 in Small Seal Script ->
    - 寺
  - **interpretation:** 寺(sì, 'temple') combines the semantic element 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), originally from 又 (yòu, 'hand'), to imply precision or holding, with the phonetic element that evolved into 士 (shì, 'scholar'). The phonetic component originally represented going or movement but later took on a more abstract form. This combination suggests a place of order and ritual, characteristic of temples.
- **examples:**
  - 他每天早晨去寺庙(廟)。
    - Tā měitiān zǎochén qù sìmiào.
    - He goes to the temple every morning.
  - 寺庙(廟)里(裡)的钟(鐘)声(聲)非常悠扬(揚)。
    - Sìmiào lǐ de zhōngshēng fēicháng yōuyáng.
    - The bell sounds in the temple are very melodious.
  - 我们(們)参(參)观(觀)了京都的古老寺庙(廟)，觉(覺)得很平静(靜)。
    - Wǒmen cānguānle Jīngdū de gǔlǎo sìmiào, juéde hěn píngjìng.
    - We visited an ancient temple in Kyoto and felt very peaceful.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 寺](@media/glyph5bfa.png)
### 等 → 寺 → 𡳿
- **definition:** to go; footprint
- **pinyin:** zhī
- **components:**
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 一
    - yī
    - the beginning place
  - 之
    - zhī
    - to go
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 止(“foot”) + 一(“the beginning place”) ->
    - originally 㞢 ->
    - similar to 出 ->
    - evolved as a variant of 之
  - **interpretation:** The character 𡳿 is a variant of 之 (zhī, "to go") and conveys the idea of movement or direction. The original form 㞢 combines 止 (zhǐ, "foot") representing a footprint with 一 (yī, "the beginning place"), symbolizing the commencement of movement or journey, leading to the meaning of 'to go'. Over time, components such as the footprint evolved into different forms, leading to variants such as 𡳿.
### 等 → 寺 → 𡳿 → 止
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 趾
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 龰
    - yù
    - stylized feet
  - 手
    - shǒu
    - hand
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Original: Foot pointing up with 3 toes and a sole ->
    - Stylized as 龰 ->
    - Derivative 趾 refers to original 'foot' meaning
  - **interpretation:** Originally depicting a footprint with toes and a sole, 止 (zhǐ, "foot") represents the foot. The character's form resembles a foot with three toes, analogous to how the hand is represented with fingers in other characters.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)的止需要静(靜)养(養)。
    - Tā shòu shāng de zhǐ xū yào jìng yǎng.
    - His injured foot needs adequate rest.
  - 他走路时(時)小心谨(謹)慎，因为(爲)止若受伤(傷)便难(難)前行。
    - Tā zǒu lù shí xiǎo xīn jǐn shèn, yīn wèi zhǐ ruò shòu shāng biàn nán qián xíng.
    - He walks carefully because if his foot gets injured, it becomes difficult to move forward.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 止](@media/glyph6b62.png)
### 等 → 寺 → 𡳿 → 止 → 趾
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 足
    - zú
    - foot
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - halt
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 足 (zú, "foot") + phonetic 止 (zhǐ) ->
    - toe
  - **interpretation:** The character combines 足 (zú, "foot"), indicating the general area involved, with 止 (zhǐ) providing the sound and potentially suggesting the idea of a part of the foot that 'halts' or 'stops' progression, which naturally leads to the notion of a toe.
- **examples:**
  - 他的脚(腳)趾受伤(傷)了。
    - Tā de jiǎozhǐ shòushāng le.
    - His toe is injured.
  - 她用脚(腳)趾轻(輕)轻(輕)地踢了一下球。
    - Tā yòng jiǎozhǐ qīngqīng de tī le yīxià qiú.
    - She gently kicked the ball with her toe.
  - 在沙滩(灘)上散步时(時)，我感受到沙子在我的脚(腳)趾间(間)流动(動)。
    - Zài shātān shàng sànbù shí, wǒ gǎnshòu dào shāzi zài wǒ de jiǎozhǐ jiān liúdòng.
    - While walking on the beach, I felt the sand flowing between my toes.
### 等 → 寺 → 𡳿 → 止 → 趾 → 足
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zú
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a leg ->
    - originally depicted as ⽦ ->
    - represents 'foot'
  - **interpretation:** The character 足(zú, 'foot') is a pictographic representation of a human leg, which directly portrays the concept of a 'foot'. The pictographic origin emphasizes its fundamental meaning in the language.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)后(後)，他的足不能动(動)。
    - tā shòushāng hòu, tā de zú bù néng dòng。
    - After he was injured, his foot couldn't move.
  - 小明打球时(時)，不小心扭伤(傷)了足。
    - xiǎo míng dǎ qiú shí, bù xiǎoxīn niǔ shāng le zú。
    - When Xiaoming was playing ball, he accidentally twisted his foot.
  - 我每天锻(鍛)炼(鍊)足部。
    - wǒ měitiān duànliàn zúbù。
    - I exercise my foot muscles every day.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 足](@media/glyph8db3.png)
### 等 → 寺 → 𡳿 → 止 → 龰
- **definition:** stylized feet
- **pinyin:** yù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a stylized footprint pointing upward ->
    - originally meaning 'foot' ->
    - later forms like 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') refer back to original meaning
  - **interpretation:** 龰 (yù, 'stylized feet') is a pictogram showing a footprint pointing up, originally indicating the concept of a foot. The character 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') evolved from this and retains the reference to the original meaning. It visually resembles a sole with three toes, similar to representations of the human hand in characters like 爪 (zhuǎ, 'claw'), 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), and 又 (yòu, 'again').
### 等 → 寺 → 𡳿 → 止 → 手
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** shǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a hand with fingers; top stroke is a bent over middle finger, horizontal strokes represent fingers
  - **interpretation:** The character 手 (shǒu, "hand") is a direct pictorial representation of a human hand with all five fingers, which distinguishes it from similar characters representing claws or simplified fingers. This visually conveys its meaning as a hand clearly.
- **examples:**
  - 他用手写(寫)字。
    - Tā yòng shǒu xiě zì.
    - He writes with his hand.
  - 妈(媽)妈(媽)牵(牽)着(著)我的手走路。
    - Māmā qiān zhe wǒ de shǒu zǒu lù.
    - Mom holds my hand while walking.
  - 他的手很温(溫)暖，带(帶)给(給)我力量。
    - Tā de shǒu hěn wēn nuǎn, dài gěi wǒ lìliàng.
    - His hand is very warm, giving me strength.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 手](@media/glyph624b.png)
### 等 → 寺 → 𡳿 → 一
- **definition:** the beginning place
- **pinyin:** yī
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:** A horizontal stroke representing the concept of 'one'.
  - **interpretation:** The character 一(yī, "one") is a simple horizontal line signifying the singular and unified concept of 'one'. It directly represents being singular or the number one.
- **examples:**
  - 我有一个(個)苹(蘋)果。
    - Wǒ yǒu yī gè píngguǒ.
    - I have one apple.
  - 他只看到一只(隻)鸟(鳥)，飞(飛)进(進)了花园(園)。
    - Tā zhǐ kàn dào yī zhī niǎo, fēi jìn le huā yuán.
    - He only saw one bird, which flew into the garden.
  - 一条(條)直路通向远(遠)方。
    - Yī tiáo zhí lù tōng xiàng yuǎn fāng.
    - One straight road leads to the distance.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 一](@media/glyph4e00.png)
### 等 → 寺 → 𡳿 → 之
- **definition:** to go
- **pinyin:** zhī
- **components:**
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 一
    - yī
    - one; the beginning place
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 止 ('foot') + 一 ('beginning place') ->
    - originally 㞢 ('to go') ->
    - simplified to a point
  - **interpretation:** The original compound 㞢 depicted a foot 止 (zhǐ, 'foot') stepping on a line 一 (yī, 'one; the beginning place'), indicating the concept of 'to go'. The footprint evolving into a point symbolized direction or movement, ultimately abstracted into 之 (zhī, 'of; possessive particle'), representing directionality or connection, as in 'of'.
- **examples:**
  - 天空之蓝(藍)让(讓)人心旷(曠)神怡。
    - Tiānkōng zhī lán ràng rén xīnkuàngshényí.
    - The blue of the sky makes people feel relaxed and happy.
  - 树(樹)之影在湖面上摇(搖)曳。
    - Shù zhī yǐng zài húmiàn shàng yáoyè.
    - The shadow of the tree sways on the surface of the lake.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 之](@media/glyph4e4b.png)
### 等 → 寺 → 寸
- **definition:** inch
- **pinyin:** cùn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - Line on the hand (ideographic) emphasizing the elbow ->
    - represents measurement unit between wrist and specific forearm position ->
    - meaning 'inch'
  - **interpretation:** 寸 (cùn, "inch") originated as a depiction of a line on the hand, indicating the area near the elbow. This specific placement was considered significant for pulse palpation, originally suggesting a forearm position, which then came to denote the measurement 'inch'.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)块(塊)布每一寸都是精心制(製)作。
    - Zhè kuài bù měi yī cùn dōu shì jīngxīn zhìzuò.
    - Every inch of this cloth is crafted with care.
  - 请(請)用卷尺量一寸，每一寸数(數)据(據)都准(準)确(確)。
    - Qǐng yòng juǎnchǐ liàng yī cùn, měi yī cùn shùjù dōu zhǔnquè.
    - Please use a tape measure to measure an inch, every inch's data is accurate.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 寸](@media/glyph5bf8.png)

## 针(針)灸
---
## acupuncture
### zhēnjiǔ
---
- **traditional:** 針灸
- **definition:** acupuncture
- **pinyin:** zhēnjiǔ
- **components:**
  - 针(針)
    - zhēn
    - needle
  - 灸
    - jiǔ
    - moxibustion
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 針 (zhēn, "needle") and 灸 (jiǔ, "moxibustion") combine to describe the practice of acupuncture, which involves using needles and heat to stimulate specific points on the body for therapeutic purposes.
  - **interpretation:** 針 (zhēn, "needle") refers to the slender pointed tool used in acupuncture, while 灸 (jiǔ, "moxibustion") involves the burning of moxa (a plant material) to create therapeutic heat. Together, 針灸 (zhēnjiǔ) denotes the combined use of both these methods to apply physical stimulation and heat to specific points on the body, based on traditional Chinese medicine principles to balance and regulate the flow of qi (vital energy).
- **examples:**
  - 他对(對)针(針)灸疗(療)法很感兴趣。
    - Tā duì zhēnjiǔ liáofǎ hěn gǎn xìngqù.
    - He is very interested in acupuncture therapy.
  - 针(針)灸可以缓(緩)解疼痛。
    - Zhēnjiǔ kěyǐ huǎnjiě téngtòng.
    - Acupuncture can relieve pain.
  - 医(醫)生建议(議)我尝(嘗)试(試)针(針)灸疗(療)法，因为(為)效果显(顯)著。
    - Yīshēng jiànyì wǒ chángshì zhēnjiǔ liáofǎ, yīnwèi xiàoguǒ xiǎnzhù.
    - The doctor suggested I try acupuncture therapy because the effects are remarkable.
### 针(針)灸 → 针(針)
- **traditional:** 針
- **definition:** needle
- **pinyin:** zhēn
- **components:**
  - 釒
    - jīn
    - metal
  - 十
    - shí
    - ten
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:** semantic 釒 (jīn, "metal") + phonetic 十 (shí)
  - **interpretation:** 釒 (jīn, "metal") indicates the material and practical use of needles being made of metal. 十 (shí) provides the phonetic component. This combination suggests a small metal object, like a needle.
  - **simplification:** Simplified by reducing 釒 (jīn, "metal") to 钅, keeping the phonetic 十 (shí) part unchanged.
- **examples:**
  - 我找不到针(針)。
    - Wǒ zhǎo bù dào zhēn.
    - I can't find the needle.
  - 医(醫)生用一根细(細)针(針)给(給)我打针(針)。
    - Yīshēng yòng yī gēn xì zhēn gěi wǒ dǎ zhēn.
    - The doctor used a thin needle to give me an injection.
  - 这(這)枚针(針)是用来(來)缝(縫)衣服的。
    - Zhè méi zhēn shì yòng lái féng yīfú de.
    - This needle is used for sewing clothes.
### 针(針)灸 → 针(針) → 釒
- **definition:** metal
- **pinyin:** jīn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts metal or gold with two nuggets on the sides and vertical lines representing gleaming or brightness ->
    - metal elements
  - **interpretation:** It visually represents pieces of metal or gold, suggesting the value and substance associated with metals, particularly gold, due to its shine and durability.
### 针(針)灸 → 针(針) → 十
- **definition:** ten
- **pinyin:** shí
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Original vertical stroke ->
    - later horizontal stroke added ->
    - forms a cross ->
    - represents 'ten'
  - **interpretation:** The character 十(shí, 'ten') represents the number ten with a cross shape that could be seen as tally marks. It evolved from a simple vertical stroke to a cross by adding a horizontal stroke, symbolizing a complete set of ten.
- **examples:**
  - 我有十本书(書)。
    - Wǒ yǒu shí běn shū.
    - I have ten books.
  - 花园(園)里(裡)有十棵树(樹)，景色十分优(優)美。
    - Huāyuán lǐ yǒu shí kē shù, jǐngsè shífēn yōuměi.
    - There are ten trees in the garden, and the scenery is very beautiful.
  - 十年磨一剑(劍)。
    - Shí nián mó yī jiàn.
    - It takes ten years of practice to hone a sword.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 十](@media/glyph5341.png)
### 针(針)灸 → 灸
- **definition:** moxibustion
- **pinyin:** jiǔ
- **components:**
  - 火
    - huǒ
    - fire
  - 久
    - jiǔ
    - long time
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 火 (huǒ, "fire") + phonetic 久 (jiǔ) ->
    - meaning
  - **interpretation:** The character 灸 (jiǔ, "moxibustion") combines the semantic 火 (huǒ, "fire") with the phonetic 久 (jiǔ) to signify the practice of applying fire or heat, particularly in traditional Chinese medicine. The 火 component directly refers to the application of heat, while 久 helps to provide the pronunciation.
- **examples:**
  - 她最近在学(學)习(習)灸法。
    - Tā zuìjìn zài xuéxí jiǔfǎ.
    - She has recently been studying the art of moxibustion.
  - 医(醫)生建议(議)我试(試)试(試)灸疗(療)，来(來)缓(緩)解腰痛。
    - Yīshēng jiànyì wǒ shìshì jiǔliáo, lái huǎnjiě yāotòng.
    - The doctor suggested I try moxibustion to alleviate back pain.
  - 在中医(醫)中，灸是一种(種)常用的疗(療)法。
    - Zài zhōngyī zhōng, jiǔ shì yī zhǒng chángyòng de liáofǎ.
    - In traditional Chinese medicine, moxibustion is a common treatment method.
### 针(針)灸 → 灸 → 火
- **definition:** fire
- **pinyin:** huǒ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts flames rising from a fire
  - **interpretation:** The character 火 (huǒ, "fire") visually represents flames flickering upwards, which intuitively conveys the essence of fire. This simple depiction is an effective way to capture the dynamic and essential nature of fire.
- **examples:**
  - 火在壁炉(爐)中熊熊燃烧(燒)。
    - Huǒ zài bìlú zhōng xióngxióng ránshāo.
    - The fire burns fiercely in the fireplace.
  - 野外露营(營)时(時)，火能驱(驅)走寒冷。
    - Yěwài lùyíng shí, huǒ néng qūzǒu hánlěng.
    - When camping outdoors, the fire can drive away the cold.
  - 遇到火灾(災)时(時)，迅速疏散最为(為)重要。
    - Yù dào huǒzāi shí, xùnsù shū sàn zuìwéi zhòngyào.
    - In case of a fire, evacuating quickly is of utmost importance.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 火](@media/glyph706b.png)
### 针(針)灸 → 灸 → 久
- **definition:** long time
- **pinyin:** jiǔ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a person bending the lower back ->
    - extended time
  - **interpretation:** The character 久 (jiǔ, "long time") visually represents a person leaning forward, symbolizing the passage of a significant amount of time. The bending posture suggests protracted duration.
- **examples:**
  - 我等待了很久。
    - Wǒ děngdài le hěn jiǔ.
    - I waited for a long time.
  - 分别(別)了很久，朋友仍然相聚。
    - Fēnbié le hěn jiǔ, péngyǒu réngrán xiāngjù.
    - It has been a long time since we parted, yet friends still meet.
  - 远(遠)行归(歸)来(來)已久，家门(門)依旧(舊)温(溫)暖。
    - Yuǎnxíng guīlái yǐ jiǔ, jiāmén yījiù wēnnuǎn.
    - It has been a long time since returning from a journey, yet the home remains welcoming.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 久](@media/glyph4e45.png)

## 下班
---
## to get off work
### xiàbān
---
- **definition:** to get off work
- **pinyin:** xiàbān
- **components:**
  - 下
    - xià
    - below; down
  - 班
    - bān
    - shift; work
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:**
    - 下 (xià, "below; down") + 班 (bān, "shift; work") =
    - to get off work ->
    - when the work shift or period is over
  - **interpretation:** 下 (xià, "below; down") indicates finishing or concluding a task, while 班 (bān, "shift; work") refers to a work period. Together, 下班 (xiàbān, "to get off work") describes the action of completing your work shift and leaving your workplace.
- **examples:**
  - 我下午五点(點)下班。
    - Wǒ xiàwǔ wǔ diǎn xiàbān.
    - I get off work at five in the afternoon.
  - 今天工作很辛苦，下班后(後)他喝了一杯咖啡。
    - Jīntiān gōngzuò hěn xīnkǔ, xiàbān hòu tā hē le yī bēi kāfēi.
    - Today work is arduous; after getting off work, he had a cup of coffee.
  - 公交车(車)缓(緩)缓(緩)驶(駛)来(來)，下班的人群开(開)始涌(湧)动(動)。
    - Gōngjiāo chē huǎn huǎn shǐ lái, xiàbān de rénqún kāishǐ yǒngdòng.
    - The bus slowly arrives, and the crowd getting off work begins to surge.
### 下班 → 下
- **definition:** below; down
- **pinyin:** xià
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - a line below another ->
    - later evolved into 下
  - **interpretation:** The character 下(xià, 'down') is an ideogram showing a line positioned below another line, visually representing 'below' or 'downward'. This layout intuitively depicts the concept of being beneath or beneath another object.
- **examples:**
  - 水从(從)山上流下。
    - Shuǐ cóng shān shàng liú xià.
    - The water flows down from the mountain.
  - 他坐下来(來)看书(書)。
    - Tā zuò xià lái kàn shū.
    - He sits down to read a book.
  - 请(請)把箱子放在地下。
    - Qǐng bǎ xiāngzi fàng zài dìxià.
    - Please put the box down on the ground.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 下](@media/glyph4e0b.png)
### 下班 → 班
- **definition:** shift; work
- **pinyin:** bān
- **components:**
  - 玨
    - jué
    - pieces of jade
  - 刀
    - dāo
    - knife
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 玨 (jué, "pieces of jade") + 刀 (dāo, "knife") ->
    - to cut jade into pieces with a knife ->
    - shift; work
  - **interpretation:** The character 班(bān, "shift; work") originally depicted the action of cutting a piece of jade into parts with a knife. Just as jade is divided into smaller parts, work or tasks are divided into shifts or segments, bridging the concept of dividing valuable items and dividing time or tasks.
- **examples:**
  - 我今天的班结(結)束后(後)我们(們)去喝饮(飲)料。
    - Wǒ jīntiān de bān jiéshù hòu wǒmen qù hē yǐnliào.
    - After my shift ends today, we will go for drinks.
  - 他新换(換)了一个(個)班，觉(覺)得很适(適)应(應)。
    - Tā xīn huànle yī gè bān, juéde hěn shìyìng.
    - He has switched to a new shift and feels very adapted to it.
  - 这(這)个(個)班的工作时(時)间(間)很长(長)，但是报(報)酬不错(錯)。
    - Zhège bān de gōngzuò shíjiān hěn cháng, dànshì bàochóu bùcuò.
    - This shift has long working hours, but the pay is good.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 班](@media/glyph73ed.png)
### 下班 → 班 → 玨
- **definition:** pieces of jade
- **pinyin:** jué
- **components:**
  - 玉
    - yù
    - jade
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 玉 ('jade') + 玉 ('jade') =
    - duplication of jade ->
    - strings of jade
  - **interpretation:** The character 玨 is an ideogrammic compound formed by the repetition of 玉 (yù, 'jade'), with the two components signifying multiple pieces or strings of jade, representing abundance or multiplicity.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 玨](@media/glyph73a8.png)
### 下班 → 班 → 玨 → 玉
- **definition:** jade
- **pinyin:** yù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a picture of a cong (琮), a sort of ritual jade totem ->
    - dot added to differentiate from 王 (wáng, "king") ->
    - final form 玉 (yù, "jade")
  - **interpretation:** The character represents a picture of a jade cong, emphasizing its role in rituals and its cultural significance. The image eventually included a distinguishing dot to ensure clarity from similar characters like 王, underscoring the value jade held as a material in ancient contexts.
- **examples:**
  - 她收到了一个漂亮的玉手镯(鐲)。
    - Tā shōu dào le yī gè piàoliang de yù shǒuzhuó.
    - She received a beautiful jade bracelet.
  - 皇帝的王冠上镶(鑲)嵌着(著)闪(閃)耀的玉石。
    - Huángdì de wángguān shàng xiāngqiànzhe shǎnyào de yùshí.
    - The emperor's crown was inlaid with shining jade stones.
  - 古代的玉器常常被视(視)为(為)珍贵(貴)的艺(藝)术(術)品。
    - Gǔdài de yùqì chángcháng bèi shìwéi zhēnguì de yìshùpǐn.
    - Ancient jade artifacts are often regarded as precious works of art.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 玉](@media/glyph7389.png)
### 下班 → 班 → 刀
- **definition:** knife
- **pinyin:** dāo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a knife
  - **interpretation:** 刀 (dāo, "knife") is a pictographic representation of a knife or blade, with a sharp edge and a handle, resembling the form of a basic cutting tool.
- **examples:**
  - 他用锋(鋒)利的刀，切开(開)蔬菜。
    - tā yòng fēnglì de dāo, qiē kāi shūcài.
    - He uses a sharp knife to cut vegetables.
  - 这(這)把刀非常锋(鋒)利。
    - zhè bǎ dāo fēicháng fēnglì.
    - This knife is very sharp.
  - 厨(廚)师(師)小心地持刀，为(為)客人切肉。
    - chúshī xiǎoxīn de chí dāo, wèi kèrén qiē ròu.
    - The chef holds the knife carefully and slices meat for the guest.
- **historical forms:**

## 中医(醫)
---
## Chinese medicine
### zhōngyī
---
- **traditional:** 中醫
- **definition:** Chinese medicine
- **pinyin:** zhōngyī
- **components:**
  - 中
    - zhōng
    - middle; central; center; China
  - 医(醫)
    - yī
    - medicine; doctor; medical service; cure
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 中 (zhōng, "middle") refers to central or middle, often alluding to the idea of China being the 'Middle Kingdom'. 醫 (yī, "medicine") refers to the practice or profession concerned with maintaining health and treating diseases.
  - **interpretation:** 中 (zhōng, "middle") suggests the central or original place where this medical practice originated, implying its association with China. 醫 (yī, "medicine") directly denotes the practice of medicine. Together, 中醫 (zhōngyī, "Chinese medicine") refers specifically to the traditional practices and methodologies of medicine developed in China.
- **examples:**
  - 中医(醫)注重整体(體)观(觀)念。
    - Zhōngyī zhùzhòng zhěngtǐ guānniàn.
    - Chinese medicine emphasizes a holistic approach.
  - 很多人都相信中医(醫)，因为(為)它有几(幾)千年的历(歷)史。
    - Hěnduō rén dōu xiāngxìn zhōngyī, yīnwèi tā yǒu jǐ qiān nián de lìshǐ.
    - Many people trust Chinese medicine because it has thousands of years of history.
  - 她在学(學)习(習)中医(醫)，希望帮(幫)助更多人。
    - Tā zài xuéxí zhōngyī, xīwàng bāngzhù gèng duō rén.
    - She is studying Chinese medicine, hoping to help more people.
### 中医(醫) → 中
- **definition:** middle; central; center; China
- **pinyin:** zhōng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an arrow piercing through the center of a target
  - **interpretation:** The character 中 (zhōng, "middle") visually represents an arrow passing through the central point of a target, illustrating the concept of 'center' or 'middle' effectively. This visual imagery is straightforward and memorable, corresponding closely with its meaning of being at the center or middle of something.
- **examples:**
  - 他站在道路中，看着(著)远(遠)方。
    - tā zhàn zài dàolù zhōng, kànzhe yuǎnfāng.
    - He stands in the middle of the road, gazing into the distance.
  - 房间(間)正中，挂(掛)着(著)一幅名画(畫)。
    - fángjiān zhèng zhōng, guàzhe yī fú mínghuà.
    - A famous painting hangs in the exact center of the room.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 中](@media/glyph4e2d.png)
### 中医(醫) → 医(醫)
- **traditional:** 醫
- **definition:** medicine; doctor; medical service; cure
- **pinyin:** yī
- **components:**
  - 匸
    - xì
    - that which hides; that which stores
  - 矢
    - shǐ
    - arrow
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 匸 (that which hides) + 矢 (arrow) =
    - a hidden arrow ->
    - metaphor for treating (hidden dangers addressed by medicine)
  - **interpretation:** The character combines the concepts of 'hide' with 'arrow', suggesting the idea of dealing with hidden threats or illnesses, akin to specialized knowledge required for healing.
  - **simplification:** 醫 was simplified by using the right side 耂 (lǎo), an abbreviated structure representing the character.
- **examples:**
  - 他是一名优(優)秀的医(醫)生。
    - Tā shì yì míng yōuxiù de yīshēng.
    - He is an excellent doctor.
  - 我感冒了，需要去医(醫)院。
    - Wǒ gǎnmào le, xūyào qù yīyuàn.
    - I caught a cold and need to go to the hospital.
  - 这(這)家医(醫)院以先进(進)的医(醫)疗(療)技术(術)闻(聞)名。
    - Zhè jiā yīyuàn yǐ xiānjìn de yīliáo jìshù wénmíng.
    - This hospital is famous for its advanced medical technology.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 医](@media/glyph533b.png)
### 中医(醫) → 医(醫) → 匸
- **definition:** that which hides; that which stores
- **pinyin:** xì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 𠃊 (symbolic graphic) ->
    - depicts an enclosure hiding something or someone ->
    - evolved to represent a concealed space or item
  - **interpretation:** The character 匸(xì, 'box') is a pictogram representing a concealed or enclosed space. Its graphical form suggests something contained or hidden, which aligns with its meaning as a 'box' or an enclosure. Unlike other related pictograms that depict physical containers, 匸 emphasizes the aspect of concealment or secrecy.
- **examples:**
  - 他把匸搬到了房间(間)角落。
    - Tā bǎ xì bān dào le fángjiān jiǎoluò.
    - He moved the box to the corner of the room.
  - 我们(們)在仓(倉)库(庫)找到了匸，里(裡)面装(裝)有秘密文件。
    - Wǒmen zài cāngkù zhǎodào le xì, lǐmiàn zhuāng yǒu mìmì wénjiàn.
    - We found the box in the warehouse, and it contained secret documents.
  - 工厂(廠)工人把旧(舊)匸清理了，然后(後)再利用。
    - Gōngchǎng gōngrén bǎ jiù xì qīnglǐ le, ránhòu zài lìyòng.
    - Factory workers cleaned the old box and then reused it.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 匸](@media/glyph5338.png)
### 中医(醫) → 医(醫) → 矢
- **definition:** arrow
- **pinyin:** shǐ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an arrow
  - **interpretation:** The character 矢(shǐ, 'arrow') is a pictogram representing an arrow. Its resemblance to arrows was more evident in ancient script forms.
- **examples:**
  - 他拉开(開)弓，射出一支矢。
    - Tā lā kāi gōng, shè chū yī zhī shǐ.
    - He drew his bow and released an arrow.
  - 古代战(戰)士用矢，攻破敌(敵)阵(陣)。
    - Gǔdài zhànshì yòng shǐ, gōng pò dí zhèn.
    - Ancient warriors used arrows to breach enemy formations.

## 页(頁)
---
## page
### yè
---
- **traditional:** 頁
- **definition:** page
- **pinyin:** yè
- **components:**
  - 首
    - shǒu
    - head
  - 卩
    - jié
    - kneeling person
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 首 (shǒu, "head") + 卩 (jié, "kneeling person") =
    - head of a kneeling person ->
    - head ->
    - later adopted for "page"
  - **interpretation:** Originally depicting the head of a kneeling person, 頁 (yè, "head") transitioned from describing a physical head to denote a "page" or "sheet," connecting the idea of a main part of a document or book.
  - **simplification:** 页(頁): The character was simplified from 頁 to 页 by retaining essential strokes, emphasizing cursive efficiency.
- **examples:**
  - 我翻开(開)书(書)，读(讀)到第一页(頁)。
    - Wǒ fān kāi shū, dú dào dì yī yè.
    - I opened the book and read the first page.
  - 他在古籍中找到了很多页(頁)，记(記)录(錄)着(著)历(歷)史秘密。
    - Tā zài gǔjí zhōng zhǎo dào le hěn duō yè, jìlù zhe lìshǐ mìmì.
    - He found many pages in the ancient texts that record historical secrets.
### 页(頁) → 首
- **definition:** head
- **pinyin:** shǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts the head of an animal with a long mouth and horns, often shown with or without hair ( 巛) ->
    - perpetuated as 𩠐 (form with hair) ->
    - streamlined to 首
  - **interpretation:** The character depicts the head of an animal, with prominent features like a long mouth and horns, emphasizing the notion of a 'head' both physically and symbolically as the foremost part.
- **examples:**
  - 他是这(這)个(個)团(團)队(隊)的首领(領)。
    - Tā shì zhège tuánduì de shǒulǐng.
    - He is the head of this team.
  - 这(這)首歌是我最喜欢(歡)的歌曲。
    - Zhè shǒu gē shì wǒ zuì xǐhuān de gēqǔ.
    - This song is my favorite track.
  - 他抬起头(頭)，看向远(遠)方的山。
    - Tā tái qǐ tóu, kàn xiàng yuǎnfāng de shān.
    - He raised his head and looked towards the distant mountains.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 首](@media/glyph9996.png)
### 页(頁) → 卩
- **definition:** kneeling person
- **pinyin:** jié
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a kneeling person from sideview
  - **interpretation:** The character 卩 (jié, "kneeling person") is a simple pictogram showing the silhouette of a person kneeling. It is unrelated to other kneeling or similar figures in different contexts such as 欠 (qiàn, "yawn") where the mouth is open, or 女 (nǚ, "woman") where the figure represents a female. Its form is solely based on the posture of kneeling.
- **examples:**
  - 那位卩正虔诚(誠)祈祷(禱)。
    - Nà wèi jié zhèng qiánchéng qídǎo.
    - That kneeling person is praying devoutly.
  - 礼(禮)仪(儀)师(師)指出，卩代表谦(謙)卑与(與)敬意。
    - Lǐyí shī zhǐchū, jié dàibiǎo qiānbēi yǔ jìngyì.
    - The ritual master pointed out that the kneeling person represents humility and respect.
  - 在庄(莊)严(嚴)仪(儀)式中，卩象征(徵)着(著)内(內)心的虔敬。
    - Zài zhuāngyán yíshì zhōng, jié xiàngzhēngzhe nèixīn de qiánjìng.
    - In the solemn ceremony, the kneeling figure symbolizes inner devotion.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 卩](@media/glyph5369.png)

## 的
---
## possessive particle
### de
---
- **definition:** possessive particle
- **pinyin:** de
- **components:**
  - 白
    - bái
    - white
  - 勺
    - sháo
    - spoon
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 白 (bái, "white") + phonetic 勺 (sháo) ->
    - possessive/attributive particle
  - **interpretation:** The character 的 originally combined 白 (bái, "white") as the semantic element, denoting brightness or clarity, with 勺 (sháo), providing the phonetic component for sound. Over time, the meaning shifted from this literal sense to function as a grammatical particle marking possession or attribution, likely due to a sound borrowing or figurative extension from the clarity or specification inherent in 'white.'
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)是我的书(書)。
    - Zhè shì wǒ de shū.
    - This is my book.
  - 他的新车(車)很漂亮。
    - Tā de xīn chē hěn piàoliang.
    - His new car is very beautiful.
  - 我喜欢(歡)听(聽)大海的声(聲)音。
    - Wǒ xǐhuān tīng dàhǎi de shēngyīn.
    - I like listening to the sound of the sea.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 的](@media/glyph7684.png)
### 的 → 白
- **definition:** white
- **pinyin:** bái
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts an acorn ->
    - white from the color of acorn's inside
  - **interpretation:** The character 白(bái, "white") is thought to depict an acorn, as suggested by its use in words related to oak and acorns. The character's meaning of "white" is likely derived from the white color of an acorn's interior.
- **examples:**
  - 白色是我最喜欢(歡)的颜(顏)色。
    - Báisè shì wǒ zuì xǐhuān de yánsè.
    - White is my favorite color.
  - 他的头(頭)发(髮)已经(經)全白了。
    - Tā de tóufà yǐjīng quán bái le.
    - His hair has turned completely white.
  - 在阳(陽)光下，白沙滩(灘)显(顯)得格外美丽(麗)。
    - Zài yángguāng xià, bái shātān xiǎnde géwài měilì.
    - In the sunlight, the white sandy beach looks especially beautiful.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 白](@media/glyph767d.png)
### 的 → 勺
- **definition:** spoon
- **pinyin:** sháo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a ladle or spoon with a long handle.
  - **interpretation:** The character 勺 (sháo, "spoon") visually resembles a spoon or ladle, representing its shape with a curved section for scooping and a handle.
- **examples:**
  - 勺是一种(種)常见(見)的餐具。
    - Sháo shì yī zhǒng chángjiàn de cānjù.
    - A spoon is a common piece of tableware.
  - 妈(媽)妈(媽)用勺，给(給)宝(寶)宝(寶)喂饭(飯)。
    - Māmā yòng sháo, gěi bǎobǎo wèi fàn.
    - Mom uses a spoon to feed the baby.
  - 我喜欢(歡)这(這)把有花纹(紋)的勺，它很特别(別)。
    - Wǒ xǐhuan zhè bǎ yǒu huāwén de sháo, tā hěn tèbié.
    - I like this patterned spoon; it is very special.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 勺](@media/glyph52fa.png)

## 的

## possessive particle
%%%
## 得
---
## must
### děi
---
- **definition:** must
- **pinyin:** děi
- **components:**
  - 貝
    - bèi
    - cowry
  - 又
    - yòu
    - hand
  - 彳
    - chì
    - step
  - 寸
    - cùn
    - inch
  - 旦
    - dàn
    - dawn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 貝 (bèi, 'cowry') + 又 (yòu, 'hand') ->
    - obtaining valuables ->
    - 彳 (chì, 'step') added, 又 changed to 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), 貝 corrupted to 旦 (dàn, 'dawn') ->
    - final form
  - **interpretation:** The character originated as a depiction of a hand picking up a cowry, symbolizing 'obtaining' valuables. The 彳 (chì, 'step') was added to suggest movement on a road, enhancing the idea of acquisition. Over time, script evolutions saw substitute elements: the component 又 (yòu, 'hand') changed to 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), reflecting the Qin script's tendency, and 貝 (bèi, 'cowry') was simplified to 旦 (dàn, 'dawn'). These changes led to the character's modern form. This transition mirrors the evolved meanings in usage: 'to get', from obtaining something physically; 'must', representing the necessity of movement or action; and its role as a structural particle in grammar for completion or necessity in expressions.
  - **simplification:** In simplified form, 得 remains unchanged from its traditional representation.
- **examples:**
  - 他跑得很快。
    - Tā pǎo de hěn kuài.
    - He runs very fast.
  - 我得去工作。
    - Wǒ děi qù gōngzuò.
    - I have to go to work.
  - 她昨天赢(贏)得了比赛(賽)。
    - Tā zuótiān yíngdé le bǐsài.
    - She won the competition yesterday.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 得](@media/glyph5f97.png)
### 得 → 貝
- **definition:** cowry
- **pinyin:** bèi
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a cowrie shell ->
    - used as currency in ancient China ->
    - stylized as 貝
  - **interpretation:** The character 貝(bèi, 'shell/money') visually represents a cowrie shell, which was used as a form of currency in ancient China. This explains why it is associated with money or valuables.
  - **simplification:** 贝 is a cursive script simplification of 貝, transforming the character into a more streamlined form while retaining its essence.
- **examples:**
  - 他把贝(貝)当作护(護)身符，放在口袋里(裡)。
    - Tā bǎ bèi dāng zuò hùshēn fú, fàng zài kǒudài lǐ.
    - He uses shells as a talisman, placing them in his pocket.
  - 古代人用贝(貝)作为(為)货(貨)币(幣)。
    - Gǔdài rén yòng bèi zuòwéi huòbì.
    - In ancient times, people used shells as currency.
### 得 → 又
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** yòu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a right hand
  - **interpretation:** The character 又 (yòu, "hand") is a pictogram representing a right hand, showing the fingers and palm, which highlights its original meaning related to manual actions.
- **examples:**
  - 「又」这(這)个(個)字最早来(來)源于(於)手。
    - 「Yòu」 zhè gè zì zuì zǎo láiyuán yú shǒu。
    - The character '又' originally comes from the hand.
  - 很多汉(漢)字含有又部首，表示与(與)手有关(關)的动(動)作。
    - Hěn duō hànzì hányǒu Yòu bùshǒu, biǎoshì yǔ shǒu yǒuguān de dòngzuò。
    - Many Chinese characters include the '又' radical, indicating actions related to the hand.
  - 古人用又描绘(繪)手的形态(態)，体(體)现(現)了古汉(漢)字的独(獨)特魅力。
    - Gǔrén yòng Yòu miáohuì shǒu de xíngtài, tǐxiàn le gǔ hànzì de dútè mèilì。
    - Ancient people used '又' to depict the shape of the hand, showcasing the unique charm of ancient Chinese characters.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 又](@media/glyph53c8.png)
### 得 → 彳
- **definition:** step
- **pinyin:** chì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a foot or person walking
  - **interpretation:** 彳(chì, 'walking') visually represents steps or a person moving, suggesting the idea of walking or movement. Despite a simplified history from characters like 行(xíng, 'walk'), its pictographic heritage directly connects with the notion of stepping or proceeding.
- **examples:**
  - 他喜欢(歡)在河边(邊)慢慢地走。
    - Tā xǐhuān zài hé biān mànmàn de zǒu.
    - He likes to walk slowly by the river.
  - 我们(們)每天退出喧嚣(囂)，享受安静(靜)的散步。
    - Wǒmen měitiān tuìchū xuānxiāo, xiǎngshòu ānjìng de sànbù.
    - We withdraw from the hustle and bustle every day to enjoy a quiet walk.
  - 他常常独(獨)自彳亍于(於)公园(園)小径(徑)。
    - Tā chángcháng dúzì chìchù yú gōngyuán xiǎojìng.
    - He often walks alone on the park trails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 彳](@media/glyph5f73.png)
### 得 → 寸
- **definition:** inch
- **pinyin:** cùn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - Line on the hand (ideographic) emphasizing the elbow ->
    - represents measurement unit between wrist and specific forearm position ->
    - meaning 'inch'
  - **interpretation:** 寸 (cùn, "inch") originated as a depiction of a line on the hand, indicating the area near the elbow. This specific placement was considered significant for pulse palpation, originally suggesting a forearm position, which then came to denote the measurement 'inch'.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)块(塊)布每一寸都是精心制(製)作。
    - Zhè kuài bù měi yī cùn dōu shì jīngxīn zhìzuò.
    - Every inch of this cloth is crafted with care.
  - 请(請)用卷尺量一寸，每一寸数(數)据(據)都准(準)确(確)。
    - Qǐng yòng juǎnchǐ liàng yī cùn, měi yī cùn shùjù dōu zhǔnquè.
    - Please use a tape measure to measure an inch, every inch's data is accurate.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 寸](@media/glyph5bf8.png)
### 得 → 旦
- **definition:** dawn
- **pinyin:** dàn
- **components:**
  - 日
    - rì
    - sun
  - 丁
    - dīng
    - nail
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 日 (rì, "sun") + 丁 (dīng, "nail") =
    - sun appearing over the horizon, 丁 indicates pronunciation
  - **interpretation:** Although the original interpretation is debated, the character combines 日 (rì, "sun") and 丁 (dīng, "nail") to depict the sun rising. This is a visual representation of dawn, where the sun emerges at the horizon line.
- **examples:**
  - 破晓(曉)的旦光洒(灑)满(滿)山川。
    - Pòxiǎo de dàn guāng sǎ mǎn shānchuān.
    - The light of dawn scattered over the mountains and rivers.
  - 黎明来(來)临(臨)时(時)，旦光映红(紅)天边(邊)。
    - Límíng láilín shí, dàn guāng yìng hóng tiānbiān.
    - When dawn arrives, the light of dawn paints the sky red.
  - 在寂静(靜)的山谷中，天边(邊)的旦光预(預)告着(著)新生。
    - Zài jìjìng de shāngǔ zhōng, tiānbiān de dàn guāng yùgào zhe xīnshēng.
    - In the quiet valley, the light of dawn heralds new life.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 旦](@media/glyph65e6.png)
### 得 → 旦 → 日
- **definition:** sun
- **pinyin:** rì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts the sun; a dot or line added in the center to distinguish from similar characters e.g. 囗
  - **interpretation:** As a pictogram, 日(rì, 'sun') directly represents the sun. In ancient times, the added dot helped visually differentiate it from other characters. This is analogous to the astronomical symbol ☉ and Egyptian hieroglyph 𓇳, both depicting the sun.
- **examples:**
  - 晨曦来(來)临(臨)时(時)，日出东(東)方。
    - Chénxī láilín shí, rìchū dōngfāng.
    - At the break of dawn, the sun rises in the east.
  - 温(溫)暖的日光洒(灑)满(滿)大地。
    - Wēnnuǎn de rìguāng sǎ mǎn dàdì.
    - The warm sunlight spreads over the earth.
  - 中午时(時)分，日高挂(掛)天。
    - Zhōngwǔ shífēn, rì gāo guà tiān.
    - At noon, the sun hangs high in the sky.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 日](@media/glyph65e5.png)
### 得 → 旦 → 丁
- **definition:** nail
- **pinyin:** dīng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts the head of a nail ->
    - 丁
  - **interpretation:** The character 丁 originally depicted the head of a nail, emphasizing simplicity and directness. While it has developed other interpretations over time, such as a head or city wall, these relate to similar shapes and functions. Today, 釘 (dīng, 'nail') reflects this meaning.
- **examples:**
  - 工人熟练(練)地把丁敲进(進)了墙(牆)壁。
    - Gōngrén shúliàn de bǎ dīng qiāng jìnle qiángbì.
    - The worker skillfully hammered the nail into the wall.
  - 他精心挑选(選)了铁(鐵)质(質)丁，确(確)保家(傢)具(俱)稳(穩)固。
    - Tā jīngxīn tiāoxuǎnle tiě zhì dīng, quèbǎo jiājù wěngù.
    - He carefully selected the iron nail to ensure the furniture was stable.
  - 请(請)把散落的丁收好。
    - Qǐng bǎ sànluò de dīng shōuhǎo.
    - Please gather the scattered nails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 丁](@media/glyph4e01.png)

## 得
---
## complement marker
### de
---
- **definition:** complement marker
- **pinyin:** de
- **components:**
  - 貝
    - bèi
    - cowry
  - 又
    - yòu
    - hand
  - 彳
    - chì
    - step
  - 寸
    - cùn
    - inch
  - 旦
    - dàn
    - dawn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 貝 (bèi, 'cowry') + 又 (yòu, 'hand') ->
    - obtaining valuables ->
    - 彳 (chì, 'step') added, 又 changed to 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), 貝 corrupted to 旦 (dàn, 'dawn') ->
    - final form
  - **interpretation:** The character originated as a depiction of a hand picking up a cowry, symbolizing 'obtaining' valuables. The 彳 (chì, 'step') was added to suggest movement on a road, enhancing the idea of acquisition. Over time, script evolutions saw substitute elements: the component 又 (yòu, 'hand') changed to 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), reflecting the Qin script's tendency, and 貝 (bèi, 'cowry') was simplified to 旦 (dàn, 'dawn'). These changes led to the character's modern form. This transition mirrors the evolved meanings in usage: 'to get', from obtaining something physically; 'must', representing the necessity of movement or action; and its role as a structural particle in grammar for completion or necessity in expressions.
  - **simplification:** In simplified form, 得 remains unchanged from its traditional representation.
- **examples:**
  - 他跑得很快。
    - Tā pǎo de hěn kuài.
    - He runs very fast.
  - 我得去工作。
    - Wǒ děi qù gōngzuò.
    - I have to go to work.
  - 她昨天赢(贏)得了比赛(賽)。
    - Tā zuótiān yíngdé le bǐsài.
    - She won the competition yesterday.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 得](@media/glyph5f97.png)
### 得 → 貝
- **definition:** cowry
- **pinyin:** bèi
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a cowrie shell ->
    - used as currency in ancient China ->
    - stylized as 貝
  - **interpretation:** The character 貝(bèi, 'shell/money') visually represents a cowrie shell, which was used as a form of currency in ancient China. This explains why it is associated with money or valuables.
  - **simplification:** 贝 is a cursive script simplification of 貝, transforming the character into a more streamlined form while retaining its essence.
- **examples:**
  - 他把贝(貝)当作护(護)身符，放在口袋里(裡)。
    - Tā bǎ bèi dāng zuò hùshēn fú, fàng zài kǒudài lǐ.
    - He uses shells as a talisman, placing them in his pocket.
  - 古代人用贝(貝)作为(為)货(貨)币(幣)。
    - Gǔdài rén yòng bèi zuòwéi huòbì.
    - In ancient times, people used shells as currency.
### 得 → 又
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** yòu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a right hand
  - **interpretation:** The character 又 (yòu, "hand") is a pictogram representing a right hand, showing the fingers and palm, which highlights its original meaning related to manual actions.
- **examples:**
  - 「又」这(這)个(個)字最早来(來)源于(於)手。
    - 「Yòu」 zhè gè zì zuì zǎo láiyuán yú shǒu。
    - The character '又' originally comes from the hand.
  - 很多汉(漢)字含有又部首，表示与(與)手有关(關)的动(動)作。
    - Hěn duō hànzì hányǒu Yòu bùshǒu, biǎoshì yǔ shǒu yǒuguān de dòngzuò。
    - Many Chinese characters include the '又' radical, indicating actions related to the hand.
  - 古人用又描绘(繪)手的形态(態)，体(體)现(現)了古汉(漢)字的独(獨)特魅力。
    - Gǔrén yòng Yòu miáohuì shǒu de xíngtài, tǐxiàn le gǔ hànzì de dútè mèilì。
    - Ancient people used '又' to depict the shape of the hand, showcasing the unique charm of ancient Chinese characters.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 又](@media/glyph53c8.png)
### 得 → 彳
- **definition:** step
- **pinyin:** chì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a foot or person walking
  - **interpretation:** 彳(chì, 'walking') visually represents steps or a person moving, suggesting the idea of walking or movement. Despite a simplified history from characters like 行(xíng, 'walk'), its pictographic heritage directly connects with the notion of stepping or proceeding.
- **examples:**
  - 他喜欢(歡)在河边(邊)慢慢地走。
    - Tā xǐhuān zài hé biān mànmàn de zǒu.
    - He likes to walk slowly by the river.
  - 我们(們)每天退出喧嚣(囂)，享受安静(靜)的散步。
    - Wǒmen měitiān tuìchū xuānxiāo, xiǎngshòu ānjìng de sànbù.
    - We withdraw from the hustle and bustle every day to enjoy a quiet walk.
  - 他常常独(獨)自彳亍于(於)公园(園)小径(徑)。
    - Tā chángcháng dúzì chìchù yú gōngyuán xiǎojìng.
    - He often walks alone on the park trails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 彳](@media/glyph5f73.png)
### 得 → 寸
- **definition:** inch
- **pinyin:** cùn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - Line on the hand (ideographic) emphasizing the elbow ->
    - represents measurement unit between wrist and specific forearm position ->
    - meaning 'inch'
  - **interpretation:** 寸 (cùn, "inch") originated as a depiction of a line on the hand, indicating the area near the elbow. This specific placement was considered significant for pulse palpation, originally suggesting a forearm position, which then came to denote the measurement 'inch'.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)块(塊)布每一寸都是精心制(製)作。
    - Zhè kuài bù měi yī cùn dōu shì jīngxīn zhìzuò.
    - Every inch of this cloth is crafted with care.
  - 请(請)用卷尺量一寸，每一寸数(數)据(據)都准(準)确(確)。
    - Qǐng yòng juǎnchǐ liàng yī cùn, měi yī cùn shùjù dōu zhǔnquè.
    - Please use a tape measure to measure an inch, every inch's data is accurate.
- **historical forms:**

## complement marker
