## must
### děi
---
- **definition:** must
- **pinyin:** děi
- **components:**
  - 貝
    - bèi
    - cowry
  - 又
    - yòu
    - hand
  - 彳
    - chì
    - step
  - 寸
    - cùn
    - inch
  - 旦
    - dàn
    - dawn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 貝 (bèi, 'cowry') + 又 (yòu, 'hand') ->
    - obtaining valuables ->
    - 彳 (chì, 'step') added, 又 changed to 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), 貝 corrupted to 旦 (dàn, 'dawn') ->
    - final form
  - **interpretation:** The character originated as a depiction of a hand picking up a cowry, symbolizing 'obtaining' valuables. The 彳 (chì, 'step') was added to suggest movement on a road, enhancing the idea of acquisition. Over time, script evolutions saw substitute elements: the component 又 (yòu, 'hand') changed to 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), reflecting the Qin script's tendency, and 貝 (bèi, 'cowry') was simplified to 旦 (dàn, 'dawn'). These changes led to the character's modern form. This transition mirrors the evolved meanings in usage: 'to get', from obtaining something physically; 'must', representing the necessity of movement or action; and its role as a structural particle in grammar for completion or necessity in expressions.
  - **simplification:** In simplified form, 得 remains unchanged from its traditional representation.
- **examples:**
  - 他跑得很快。
    - Tā pǎo de hěn kuài.
    - He runs very fast.
  - 我得去工作。
    - Wǒ děi qù gōngzuò.
    - I have to go to work.
  - 她昨天赢(贏)得了比赛(賽)。
    - Tā zuótiān yíngdé le bǐsài.
    - She won the competition yesterday.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 得](@media/glyph5f97.png)
### 得 → 貝
- **definition:** cowry
- **pinyin:** bèi
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a cowrie shell ->
    - used as currency in ancient China ->
    - stylized as 貝
  - **interpretation:** The character 貝(bèi, 'shell/money') visually represents a cowrie shell, which was used as a form of currency in ancient China. This explains why it is associated with money or valuables.
  - **simplification:** 贝 is a cursive script simplification of 貝, transforming the character into a more streamlined form while retaining its essence.
- **examples:**
  - 他把贝(貝)当作护(護)身符，放在口袋里(裡)。
    - Tā bǎ bèi dāng zuò hùshēn fú, fàng zài kǒudài lǐ.
    - He uses shells as a talisman, placing them in his pocket.
  - 古代人用贝(貝)作为(為)货(貨)币(幣)。
    - Gǔdài rén yòng bèi zuòwéi huòbì.
    - In ancient times, people used shells as currency.
### 得 → 又
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** yòu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a right hand
  - **interpretation:** The character 又 (yòu, "hand") is a pictogram representing a right hand, showing the fingers and palm, which highlights its original meaning related to manual actions.
- **examples:**
  - 「又」这(這)个(個)字最早来(來)源于(於)手。
    - 「Yòu」 zhè gè zì zuì zǎo láiyuán yú shǒu。
    - The character '又' originally comes from the hand.
  - 很多汉(漢)字含有又部首，表示与(與)手有关(關)的动(動)作。
    - Hěn duō hànzì hányǒu Yòu bùshǒu, biǎoshì yǔ shǒu yǒuguān de dòngzuò。
    - Many Chinese characters include the '又' radical, indicating actions related to the hand.
  - 古人用又描绘(繪)手的形态(態)，体(體)现(現)了古汉(漢)字的独(獨)特魅力。
    - Gǔrén yòng Yòu miáohuì shǒu de xíngtài, tǐxiàn le gǔ hànzì de dútè mèilì。
    - Ancient people used '又' to depict the shape of the hand, showcasing the unique charm of ancient Chinese characters.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 又](@media/glyph53c8.png)
### 得 → 彳
- **definition:** step
- **pinyin:** chì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a foot or person walking
  - **interpretation:** 彳(chì, 'walking') visually represents steps or a person moving, suggesting the idea of walking or movement. Despite a simplified history from characters like 行(xíng, 'walk'), its pictographic heritage directly connects with the notion of stepping or proceeding.
- **examples:**
  - 他喜欢(歡)在河边(邊)慢慢地走。
    - Tā xǐhuān zài hé biān mànmàn de zǒu.
    - He likes to walk slowly by the river.
  - 我们(們)每天退出喧嚣(囂)，享受安静(靜)的散步。
    - Wǒmen měitiān tuìchū xuānxiāo, xiǎngshòu ānjìng de sànbù.
    - We withdraw from the hustle and bustle every day to enjoy a quiet walk.
  - 他常常独(獨)自彳亍于(於)公园(園)小径(徑)。
    - Tā chángcháng dúzì chìchù yú gōngyuán xiǎojìng.
    - He often walks alone on the park trails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 彳](@media/glyph5f73.png)
### 得 → 寸
- **definition:** inch
- **pinyin:** cùn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - Line on the hand (ideographic) emphasizing the elbow ->
    - represents measurement unit between wrist and specific forearm position ->
    - meaning 'inch'
  - **interpretation:** 寸 (cùn, "inch") originated as a depiction of a line on the hand, indicating the area near the elbow. This specific placement was considered significant for pulse palpation, originally suggesting a forearm position, which then came to denote the measurement 'inch'.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)块(塊)布每一寸都是精心制(製)作。
    - Zhè kuài bù měi yī cùn dōu shì jīngxīn zhìzuò.
    - Every inch of this cloth is crafted with care.
  - 请(請)用卷尺量一寸，每一寸数(數)据(據)都准(準)确(確)。
    - Qǐng yòng juǎnchǐ liàng yī cùn, měi yī cùn shùjù dōu zhǔnquè.
    - Please use a tape measure to measure an inch, every inch's data is accurate.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 寸](@media/glyph5bf8.png)
### 得 → 旦
- **definition:** dawn
- **pinyin:** dàn
- **components:**
  - 日
    - rì
    - sun
  - 丁
    - dīng
    - nail
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 日 (rì, "sun") + 丁 (dīng, "nail") =
    - sun appearing over the horizon, 丁 indicates pronunciation
  - **interpretation:** Although the original interpretation is debated, the character combines 日 (rì, "sun") and 丁 (dīng, "nail") to depict the sun rising. This is a visual representation of dawn, where the sun emerges at the horizon line.
- **examples:**
  - 破晓(曉)的旦光洒(灑)满(滿)山川。
    - Pòxiǎo de dàn guāng sǎ mǎn shānchuān.
    - The light of dawn scattered over the mountains and rivers.
  - 黎明来(來)临(臨)时(時)，旦光映红(紅)天边(邊)。
    - Límíng láilín shí, dàn guāng yìng hóng tiānbiān.
    - When dawn arrives, the light of dawn paints the sky red.
  - 在寂静(靜)的山谷中，天边(邊)的旦光预(預)告着(著)新生。
    - Zài jìjìng de shāngǔ zhōng, tiānbiān de dàn guāng yùgào zhe xīnshēng.
    - In the quiet valley, the light of dawn heralds new life.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 旦](@media/glyph65e6.png)
### 得 → 旦 → 日
- **definition:** sun
- **pinyin:** rì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts the sun; a dot or line added in the center to distinguish from similar characters e.g. 囗
  - **interpretation:** As a pictogram, 日(rì, 'sun') directly represents the sun. In ancient times, the added dot helped visually differentiate it from other characters. This is analogous to the astronomical symbol ☉ and Egyptian hieroglyph 𓇳, both depicting the sun.
- **examples:**
  - 晨曦来(來)临(臨)时(時)，日出东(東)方。
    - Chénxī láilín shí, rìchū dōngfāng.
    - At the break of dawn, the sun rises in the east.
  - 温(溫)暖的日光洒(灑)满(滿)大地。
    - Wēnnuǎn de rìguāng sǎ mǎn dàdì.
    - The warm sunlight spreads over the earth.
  - 中午时(時)分，日高挂(掛)天。
    - Zhōngwǔ shífēn, rì gāo guà tiān.
    - At noon, the sun hangs high in the sky.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 日](@media/glyph65e5.png)
### 得 → 旦 → 丁
- **definition:** nail
- **pinyin:** dīng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts the head of a nail ->
    - 丁
  - **interpretation:** The character 丁 originally depicted the head of a nail, emphasizing simplicity and directness. While it has developed other interpretations over time, such as a head or city wall, these relate to similar shapes and functions. Today, 釘 (dīng, 'nail') reflects this meaning.
- **examples:**
  - 工人熟练(練)地把丁敲进(進)了墙(牆)壁。
    - Gōngrén shúliàn de bǎ dīng qiāng jìnle qiángbì.
    - The worker skillfully hammered the nail into the wall.
  - 他精心挑选(選)了铁(鐵)质(質)丁，确(確)保家(傢)具(俱)稳(穩)固。
    - Tā jīngxīn tiāoxuǎnle tiě zhì dīng, quèbǎo jiājù wěngù.
    - He carefully selected the iron nail to ensure the furniture was stable.
  - 请(請)把散落的丁收好。
    - Qǐng bǎ sànluò de dīng shōuhǎo.
    - Please gather the scattered nails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 丁](@media/glyph4e01.png)

## 不用
---
## not need
### bú yòng
---
- **definition:** not need
- **pinyin:** bú yòng
- **components:**
  - 不
    - bù
    - not; no
  - 用
    - yòng
    - use; employ; need; consume
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 不 (bù, "not") + 用 (yòng, "use") combine to produce "not need" by conveying the idea of not using something, hence not requiring or needing it.
  - **interpretation:** The core meaning of 不用 (bùyòng, "not need") comes from combining 不 (bù, "not") and 用 (yòng, "use"). 不 (bù, "not") negates whatever follows it, while 用 (yòng, "use") refers to the act of utilizing or employing something. Together, they clearly imply "not use," which naturally extends to "not need," as need often leads to use. In this construction, 不 (bù, "not") directly negates the act implied by 用 (yòng, "use"). Therefore, in context, 不用 denotes a lack of necessity since something that is not used is typically not needed.
- **examples:**
  - 你不用担(擔)心。
    - Nǐ bú yòng dānxīn.
    - You don't need to worry.
  - 我们(們)不用买(買)票，因为(為)这(這)是免费(費)的。
    - Wǒmen bú yòng mǎi piào, yīnwèi zhè shì miǎnfèi de.
    - We don't need to buy tickets because this is free.
  - 他们(們)不用早点到。
    - Tāmen bú yòng zǎodiǎn dào.
    - They don't need to arrive early.
### 不用 → 不
- **definition:** not; no
- **pinyin:** bù
- **components:**
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
  - 否
    - fǒu
    - no
  - 柎
    - fū
    - calyx
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a calyx of a flower ->
    - used phono-semantically in 否 (fǒu, "no") with 口 (kǒu, "mouth") to express negation ->
    - borrowed back as synonym for 否 to mean "not"
  - **interpretation:** Originally depicted a calyx, the character 不 was used phonosemantically in 否 (fǒu, "no") to convey negation by combining with 口 (kǒu, "mouth"). This negation concept spread back to 不, shifting its meaning to "not". The calyx meaning is now expressed by 柎.
- **examples:**
  - 我不是医(醫)生。
    - Wǒ bú shì yīshēng.
    - I am not a doctor.
  - 他不想去公园(園)。
    - Tā bù xiǎng qù gōngyuán.
    - He doesn't want to go to the park.
  - 天气(氣)不太好，所以我们(們)待在家里(裡)。
    - Tiānqì bù tài hǎo, suǒyǐ wǒmen dāi zài jiālǐ.
    - The weather is not very good, so we stayed at home.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 不](@media/glyph4e0d.png)
### 不用 → 不 → 口
- **definition:** mouth
- **pinyin:** kǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth.
  - **interpretation:** The character 口(kǒu, 'mouth') is a straightforward pictogram that visually represents an open mouth. It is a fundamental character in the Chinese language, often used both as an independent word and as a component in more complex characters, lending a semantic association to ideas relating to speech, openings, or enclosures.
- **examples:**
  - 他张(張)开(開)口，大声(聲)喊叫。
    - Tā zhāngkāi kǒu, dàshēng hǎnjiào.
    - He opened his mouth and shouted loudly.
  - 这(這)口饭(飯)入口即化。
    - Zhè kǒu fàn rùkǒu jíhuà.
    - This mouthful of food melts in your mouth.
  - 小女孩咬了一口苹(蘋)果，露出甜美的笑容。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái yǎole yī kǒu píngguǒ, lùchū tiánměi de xiàoróng.
    - The little girl took a bite of the apple and smiled sweetly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 口](@media/glyph53e3.png)
### 不用 → 不 → 否
- **definition:** no
- **pinyin:** fǒu
- **components:**
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
  - 不
    - bù
    - not
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 口 (kǒu, "mouth") + phonetic 不 (bù, "not") ->
    - represent denial or negation
  - **interpretation:** The character 否(pǐ, "no") combines the semantic element 口 (kǒu, "mouth") with the phonetic element 不 (bù, "not"). The mouth is associated with speech, and when combined with 'not', it conveys the idea of refusal or denial, which aligns with the meaning 'no'.
- **examples:**
  - 你去不去学(學)校？
    - Nǐ qù bù qù xuéxiào?
    - Are you going to school or not?
  - 这(這)个(個)答案是对(對)的还(還)是错(錯)的？
    - Zhège dá'àn shì duì de háishì cuò de?
    - Is this answer right or wrong?
  - 他是否知道这(這)个(個)消息？
    - Tā shìfǒu zhīdào zhège xiāoxi?
    - Does he know this news or not?
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 否](@media/glyph5426.png)
### 不用 → 不 → 柎
- **definition:** calyx
- **pinyin:** fū
- **components:**
  - 木
    - mù
    - wood
  - 付
    - fù
    - to pay
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 木 (mù, "wood") + phonetic 付 (fù) ->
    - meaning
  - **interpretation:** 柎(fū, "calyx") combines 木 (mù, "wood"), which highlights the botanical context related to plants and flowers, with 付 (fù), which provides the phonetic component. The structure suggests a part of a plant, specifically the calyx, which is wooden or firm like 木 (mù, "wood").
### 不用 → 不 → 柎 → 木
- **definition:** wood
- **pinyin:** mù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a tree with branches and roots
  - **interpretation:** The character 木(mù) depicts a tree, showing the trunk in the center and two slanting lines representing branches or roots. It directly signifies the concept of wood or a tree.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)把椅子的主要材料是木。
    - Zhè bǎ yǐzi de zhǔyào cáiliào shì mù.
    - The main material of this chair is wood.
  - 工匠精心雕刻木，制成精美家具。
    - Gōngjiàng jīngxīn diāo kè mù, zhìchéng jīngměi jiājù.
    - The craftsman carefully carved the wood, crafting exquisite furniture.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 木](@media/glyph6728.png)
### 不用 → 不 → 柎 → 付
- **definition:** to pay
- **pinyin:** fù
- **components:**
  - 亻(人)
    - rén
    - person
  - 又
    - yòu
    - hand
  - 寸
    - cùn
    - hand
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 亻(人) (rén, "person") + 又 (yòu, "hand") or 亻(人) (rén, "person") + 寸 (cùn, "hand") =
    - person giving with hand ->
    - to deliver, hand over
  - **interpretation:** The character 付 (fù, "hand over") combines 亻(人) (rén, "person") with a hand component. It visually represents the action of a person handing something over to another, emphasizing the act of giving or delivering.
- **examples:**
  - 我把钱(錢)付给(給)他。
    - Wǒ bǎ qián fù gěi tā.
    - I handed the money to him.
  - 他急忙把票款付给(給)售票员(員)，以便赶(趕)上电(電)影。
    - Tā jímáng bǎ piào kuǎn fù gěi shòupiàoyuán, yǐbiàn gǎn shàng diànyǐng.
    - He hurriedly handed the ticket payment to the ticket seller to catch the movie.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 付](@media/glyph4ed8.png)
### 不用 → 不 → 柎 → 付 → 亻
- **definition:** person
- **pinyin:** rén
- **components:**
  - 人
    - rén
    - person
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Stylization of 人 (rén, "person") as a side radical to depict a person
  - **interpretation:** 亻 is a stylized form of 人 (rén, "person") used to indicate human-related meanings when combined with other components in characters as a radical. It visually represents a standing person, maintaining the core meaning of 'person' while facilitating the construction of complex characters.
- **examples:**
  - 他是一个(個)热(熱)心的人。
    - Tā shì yī gè rèxīn de rén.
    - He is a kind-hearted person.
  - 这(這)座城市里(裡)住着(著)很多优(優)秀的人。
    - Zhè zuò chéngshì lǐ zhùzhe hěn duō yōuxiù de rén.
    - There are many outstanding people living in this city.
  - 每个(個)人都有梦(夢)想。
    - Měi gè rén dōu yǒu mèngxiǎng.
    - Everyone has dreams.
### 不用 → 不 → 柎 → 付 → 亻 → 人
- **definition:** person
- **pinyin:** rén
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts side view of a standing man, highlighting an arm and a leg ->
    - visual representation of a person
  - **interpretation:** The character 人 (rén, 'person') effectively uses simple lines to depict the essential form of a human, making it immediately recognizable and intuitive as meaning 'person.'
- **examples:**
  - 他是个(個)好人。
    - Tā shì gè hǎo rén.
    - He is a good person.
  - 每个(個)人都有责(責)任，为(為)社会(會)作出贡(貢)献(獻)。
    - Měi gè rén dōu yǒu zérèn, wèi shèhuì zuòchū gòngxiàn.
    - Every person has a responsibility to contribute to society.
  - 人在旅途中，心灵(靈)获(獲)得了成长(長)。
    - Rén zài lǚtú zhōng, xīnlíng huòdé le chéngzhǎng.
    - People gain growth along their journey.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 人](@media/glyph4eba.png)
### 不用 → 不 → 柎 → 付 → 又
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** yòu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a right hand
  - **interpretation:** The character 又 (yòu, "hand") is a pictogram representing a right hand, showing the fingers and palm, which highlights its original meaning related to manual actions.
- **examples:**
  - 「又」这(這)个(個)字最早来(來)源于(於)手。
    - 「Yòu」 zhè gè zì zuì zǎo láiyuán yú shǒu。
    - The character '又' originally comes from the hand.
  - 很多汉(漢)字含有又部首，表示与(與)手有关(關)的动(動)作。
    - Hěn duō hànzì hányǒu Yòu bùshǒu, biǎoshì yǔ shǒu yǒuguān de dòngzuò。
    - Many Chinese characters include the '又' radical, indicating actions related to the hand.
  - 古人用又描绘(繪)手的形态(態)，体(體)现(現)了古汉(漢)字的独(獨)特魅力。
    - Gǔrén yòng Yòu miáohuì shǒu de xíngtài, tǐxiàn le gǔ hànzì de dútè mèilì。
    - Ancient people used '又' to depict the shape of the hand, showcasing the unique charm of ancient Chinese characters.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 又](@media/glyph53c8.png)
### 不用 → 不 → 柎 → 付 → 寸
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** cùn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - Line on the hand (ideographic) emphasizing the elbow ->
    - represents measurement unit between wrist and specific forearm position ->
    - meaning 'inch'
  - **interpretation:** 寸 (cùn, "inch") originated as a depiction of a line on the hand, indicating the area near the elbow. This specific placement was considered significant for pulse palpation, originally suggesting a forearm position, which then came to denote the measurement 'inch'.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)块(塊)布每一寸都是精心制(製)作。
    - Zhè kuài bù měi yī cùn dōu shì jīngxīn zhìzuò.
    - Every inch of this cloth is crafted with care.
  - 请(請)用卷尺量一寸，每一寸数(數)据(據)都准(準)确(確)。
    - Qǐng yòng juǎnchǐ liàng yī cùn, měi yī cùn shùjù dōu zhǔnquè.
    - Please use a tape measure to measure an inch, every inch's data is accurate.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 寸](@media/glyph5bf8.png)
### 不用 → 用
- **definition:** use; employ; need; consume
- **pinyin:** yòng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a water bucket
  - **interpretation:** The character 用(yòng, "use") originally depicted a water bucket, an essential tool for drawing water, symbolizing the concept of utilizing or employing objects or resources.
- **examples:**
  - 他用筷子吃饭(飯)。
    - Tā yòng kuàizi chīfàn.
    - He uses chopsticks to eat.
  - 请(請)用这(這)支笔(筆)写(寫)字。
    - Qǐng yòng zhè zhī bǐ xiězì.
    - Please use this pen to write.
  - 有人用手机(機)看电(電)影。
    - Yǒurén yòng shǒujī kàn diànyǐng.
    - Someone is using a phone to watch a movie.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 用](@media/glyph7528.png)

## 美元
---
## US dollar
### měiyuán
---
- **definition:** US dollar
- **pinyin:** měiyuán
- **components:**
  - 美
    - měi
    - beautiful; America
  - 元
    - yuán
    - currency unit; origin
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 美 (měi, "beautiful; America") + 元 (yuán, "currency unit; origin") creates the term for 'US dollar', emphasizing America as both the location associated with the currency and 'beautiful', which historically ties to the perception of America.
  - **interpretation:** 美 (měi, "beautiful; America") is used here as a phonetic and semantic element representing America, stemming from usage where 美洲 (měizhōu, "America") reinforces this link. 元 (yuán, "currency unit; origin") refers to money; the core or fundamental unit. The combination thus signifies the primary monetary unit of the United States.
- **examples:**
  - 我有一百美元。
    - Wǒ yǒu yì bǎi měiyuán.
    - I have one hundred US dollars.
  - 美元对(對)人民币(幣)的汇(匯)率，最近有所改变(變)。
    - Měiyuán duì rénmínbì de huìlǜ, zuìjìn yǒu suǒ gǎibiàn.
    - The exchange rate of the US dollar to RMB has changed recently.
  - 许(許)多人用美元储(儲)蓄，因为(為)它的稳(穩)定性。
    - Xǔduō rén yòng měiyuán chǔxù, yīnwèi tā de wěndìngxìng.
    - Many people save in US dollars because of its stability.
### 美元 → 美
- **definition:** beautiful; America
- **pinyin:** měi
- **components:**
  - 羊
    - yáng
    - sheep
  - 大
    - dà
    - big
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - 羊 (yáng, "sheep") + 大 (dà, "big") =
    - a big sheep, which was seen as beautiful and auspicious ->
    - beautiful
  - **interpretation:** The combination of 羊 (yáng, "sheep") and 大 (dà, "big") reflects the cultural value of sheep as symbols of beauty and prosperity in ancient China. A large sheep was particularly prized, leading to the association with beauty.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)个(個)景色很美。
    - Zhège jǐngsè hěn měi.
    - This scenery is beautiful.
  - 她的笑容美极(極)了。
    - Tā de xiàoróng měi jí le.
    - Her smile is extremely beautiful.
  - 夜晚来(來)临(臨)时(時)，月光无(無)限美。
    - Yèwǎn láilín shí, yuèguāng wúxiàn měi.
    - When night falls, the moonlight is infinitely beautiful.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 美](@media/glyph7f8e.png)
### 美元 → 美 → 羊
- **definition:** sheep
- **pinyin:** yáng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a ram's head
  - **interpretation:** The character 羊(yáng, 'sheep') visually represents the head of a sheep or ram, capturing the animal's distinctive features. It serves as a straightforward pictogram, portraying one of the common animals in ancient agrarian societies.
- **examples:**
  - 农(農)场(場)里(裡)有羊。
    - Nóngchǎng lǐ yǒu yáng.
    - There are sheep on the farm.
  - 春天来(來)了，羊群在草地上吃草。
    - Chūntiān lái le, yángqún zài cǎodì shàng chī cǎo.
    - In spring, the flock of sheep grazes on the meadow.
  - 那只(隻)羊看起来(來)很温(溫)顺(順)。
    - Nà zhī yáng kàn qǐlái hěn wēnshùn.
    - That sheep looks very gentle.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 羊](@media/glyph7f8a.png)
### 美元 → 美 → 大
- **definition:** big
- **pinyin:** dà
- **components:**
  - 夫
    - fū
    - man
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a person facing forward ->
    - Borrowed phonetically for 'big'; original form of 夫 (fū, 'man')
  - **interpretation:** The character 大(dà) depicts a person facing forward, representing 'big' by suggesting the idea of someone standing prominently. Although often thought of as a person with outstretched arms, early scripts do not support this interpretation. It was originally the form of 夫 (fū, 'man') and was later phonetically borrowed for the meaning 'big.'
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)个(個)房子很大。
    - Zhè ge fángzi hěn dà.
    - This house is very big.
  - 大海波涛(濤)汹(洶)涌(湧)，展现(現)出大自然的力量。
    - Dàhǎi bōtāo xiōngyǒng, zhǎnxiàn chū dàzìrán de lìliàng.
    - The vast ocean waves surge, showcasing the power of nature.
  - 大人物登场(場)，留下传(傳)奇。
    - Dà rénwù dēngchǎng, liúxià chuánqí.
    - Great figures make an appearance, leaving behind legends.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 大](@media/glyph5927.png)
### 美元 → 美 → 大 → 夫
- **definition:** man
- **pinyin:** fū
- **components:**
  - 大
    - dà
    - big
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a variant form of 大 (dà, "big") representing an adult man with a hairpin ->
    - became associated with 夫 (fū, "man").
  - **interpretation:** 夫 (fū, "man") was visually similar to 大 (dà, "big") and was originally interchangeable. The addition of the horizontal stroke was interpreted as a hairpin, symbolizing adulthood for men.
- **examples:**
  - 此夫心怀(懷)大志。
    - Cǐ fū xīn huái dà zhì.
    - This man has lofty aspirations.
  - 他勤劳(勞)努力，堪称(稱)良夫。
    - Tā qín láo nǔ lì, kān chēng liáng fū.
    - He works diligently and is regarded as an exemplary man.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 夫](@media/glyph592b.png)
### 美元 → 元
- **definition:** currency unit; origin
- **pinyin:** yuán
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a human head above a horizontal line, symbolizing the origin or the head of something
  - **interpretation:** 元 (yuán, 'origin') represents the head, which is often considered the starting point or leader, aligning with the concept of 'origin'. This setup also connects metaphorically to beginnings or first principles.
- **examples:**
  - 万(萬)物之元来(來)自于(於)混沌。
    - Wànwù zhī yuán láizì yú húndùn.
    - The origin of all things comes from chaos.
  - 道家的理念追寻(尋)心灵(靈)的元。
    - Dàojiā de lǐniàn zhuīxún xīnlíng de yuán.
    - Taoist philosophy seeks the origin of the soul.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 元](@media/glyph5143.png)

## 刚(剛)
---
## just
### gāng
---
- **traditional:** 剛
- **definition:** just
- **pinyin:** gāng
- **components:**
  - 岡
    - gāng
    - mountain ridge
  - 刀
    - dāo
    - knife
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 岡 (gāng) + semantic 刀 (knife) ->
    - hard, firm
  - **interpretation:** 岡 (gāng, 'mountain ridge') provides the sound, suggesting a firm or solid structure, with 刀 (dāo, 'knife') indicating sharpness or firmness. Thus, 刚(剛) (gāng, 'firm') connotes hardness or strength, while the definite, exact nature of a firm edge lends to meanings of precise timing ('just now') and minimal sufficiency ('barely').
  - **simplification:** 剛 (gāng, 'firm') was simplified to 刚(剛) by replacing the phonetic 岡 (gāng, 'mountain ridge') with 冈, retaining the knife radical 刀.
- **examples:**
  - 我刚(剛)吃完晚饭(飯)。
    - Wǒ gāng chī wán wǎnfàn.
    - I just finished dinner.
  - 他刚(剛)走进(進)教室，铃(鈴)声(聲)就响(響)了。
    - Tā gāng zǒu jìn jiàoshì, língshēng jiù xiǎng le.
    - He just entered the classroom when the bell rang.
  - 这(這)个(個)盒子很坚(堅)硬，像石头(頭)一样(樣)。
    - Zhège hézi hěn jiānyìng, xiàng shítou yīyàng.
    - This box is very hard, like a stone.
### 刚(剛) → 岡
- **definition:** mountain ridge
- **pinyin:** gāng
- **components:**
  - 网(網)
    - mǎng
    - net
  - 山
    - shān
    - mountain
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 网 (mǎng) + semantic 山 (shān, "mountain") ->
    - ridge
  - **interpretation:** The character combines the semantic 山 (shān, "mountain") suggesting a topographical feature, with the phonetic 网 (mǎng) to provide the sound. A ridge is a prominent mountain feature, making this combination intuitive for indicating 'ridge'.
- **examples:**
  - 那座高冈(岡)，是徒步旅行的好地方。
    - Nà zuò gāo gāng, shì túbù lǚxíng de hǎo dìfāng.
    - That high ridge is a great place for hiking.
  - 太阳(陽)从(從)山冈(岡)升起，洒(灑)下金色的光芒。
    - Tàiyáng cóng shān gāng shēng qǐ, sǎ xià jīnsè de guāngmáng.
    - The sun rises from the ridge, casting golden rays.
  - 在冈(岡)顶(頂)上，你可以看到整个(個)村庄(莊)。
    - Zài gāng dǐng shàng, nǐ kěyǐ kàn dào zhěnggè cūnzhuāng.
    - On the top of the ridge, you can see the entire village.
### 刚(剛) → 岡 → 网(網)
- **traditional:** 網
- **definition:** net
- **pinyin:** mǎng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a net with crossing lines or mesh ->
    - symbol for 'net'
  - **interpretation:** The character 网(網) (wǎng, 'net') visually represents a net with lines intersecting to form a grid, making it intuitive as a symbol for a net or mesh.
  - **simplification:** The simplified character 网 (wǎng) retains the essential visual structure of intersecting lines to depict a net. It conveys the idea of a net through a simplified representation without additional semantic or phonetic elements.
- **examples:**
  - 他用网(網)捕鱼(魚)，快乐(樂)满(滿)怀(懷)。
    - Tā yòng wǎng bǔ yú, kuàilè mǎn huái.
    - He fishes with a net and is full of joy.
  - 很多信息通过(過)网(網)传(傳)播，速度惊(驚)人。
    - Hěn duō xìnxī tōngguò wǎng chuánbō, sùdù jīngrén.
    - A lot of information spreads through the net with astonishing speed.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 网](@media/glyph7f51.png)
### 刚(剛) → 岡 → 山
- **definition:** mountain
- **pinyin:** shān
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts three mountain peaks
  - **interpretation:** The character 山(shān, "mountain") visually represents the concept of a mountain using three vertical lines that suggest peaks. This depiction is consistent with early forms found in Oracle Bone Script, emphasizing the notion of natural elevation associated with mountains.
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)去爬山。
    - Wǒmen qù pá shān.
    - We go climb the mountain.
  - 那座大山让(讓)人惊(驚)叹(嘆)。
    - Nà zuò dà shān ràng rén jīngtàn.
    - That mountain astonishes people.
  - 远(遠)处(處)的山隐(隱)约(約)在云(雲)中，令人心旷(曠)神怡。
    - Yuǎnchù de shān yǐnyuē zài yún zhōng, lìng rén xīnkuàng shényí.
    - The distant mountain fades into the clouds, leaving one in a state of peace.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 山](@media/glyph5c71.png)
### 刚(剛) → 刀
- **definition:** knife
- **pinyin:** dāo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a knife
  - **interpretation:** 刀 (dāo, "knife") is a pictographic representation of a knife or blade, with a sharp edge and a handle, resembling the form of a basic cutting tool.
- **examples:**
  - 他用锋(鋒)利的刀，切开(開)蔬菜。
    - tā yòng fēnglì de dāo, qiē kāi shūcài.
    - He uses a sharp knife to cut vegetables.
  - 这(這)把刀非常锋(鋒)利。
    - zhè bǎ dāo fēicháng fēnglì.
    - This knife is very sharp.
  - 厨(廚)师(師)小心地持刀，为(為)客人切肉。
    - chúshī xiǎoxīn de chí dāo, wèi kèrén qiē ròu.
    - The chef holds the knife carefully and slices meat for the guest.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 刀](@media/glyph5200.png)
---
## 刚(剛)
### gāng

## 刚(剛)刚(剛)
---
## just now
### gānggāng
---
- **traditional:** 剛剛
- **definition:** just now
- **pinyin:** gānggāng
- **components:**
  - 刚(剛)
    - gāng
    - just; firm
  - 刚(剛)
    - gāng
    - just; firm
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 刚(剛) (gāng, "just; firm") + 刚(剛) (gāng, "just; firm") reinforce the sense of immediacy or recent occurrence.
  - **interpretation:** The repetition of 刚(剛) (gāng, "just; firm") emphasizes the idea of something having happened very recently or just moments before. This concept is reflected in its common use to indicate 'just now' or 'just recently' in time expressions. The doubling intensifies the immediacy.
- **examples:**
  - 他刚(剛)刚(剛)走。
    - Tā gānggāng zǒu.
    - He just left.
  - 我刚(剛)刚(剛)到了，看到朋友站在门(門)外。
    - Wǒ gānggāng dào le, kàn dào péngyǒu zhàn zài ménwài.
    - I just arrived and saw a friend standing outside the door.

- **historical forms:**

### 刚(剛)刚(剛) → 刚(剛) → 岡 → 山
- **definition:** mountain
- **pinyin:** shān
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts three mountain peaks
  - **interpretation:** The character 山(shān, "mountain") visually represents the concept of a mountain using three vertical lines that suggest peaks. This depiction is consistent with early forms found in Oracle Bone Script, emphasizing the notion of natural elevation associated with mountains.
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)去爬山。
    - Wǒmen qù pá shān.
    - We go climb the mountain.
  - 那座大山让(讓)人惊(驚)叹(嘆)。
    - Nà zuò dà shān ràng rén jīngtàn.
    - That mountain astonishes people.
  - 远(遠)处(處)的山隐(隱)约(約)在云(雲)中，令人心旷(曠)神怡。
    - Yuǎnchù de shān yǐnyuē zài yún zhōng, lìng rén xīnkuàng shényí.
    - The distant mountain fades into the clouds, leaving one in a state of peace.

  - **description:** Depicts a knife
  - **interpretation:** 刀 (dāo, "knife") is a pictographic representation of a knife or blade, with a sharp edge and a handle, resembling the form of a basic cutting tool.
- **examples:**
  - 他用锋(鋒)利的刀，切开(開)蔬菜。

  - 厨(廚)师(師)小心地持刀，为(為)客人切肉。
    - chúshī xiǎoxīn de chí dāo, wèi kèrén qiē ròu.

## 星期天
---
## Sunday
### xīngqītiān
---
- **definition:** Sunday
- **pinyin:** xīngqītiān
- **components:**
  - 星
    - xīng
    - star
  - 期
    - qī
    - period; phase; time
  - 天
    - tiān
    - day; sky
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 星 (xīng, "star") + 期 (qī, "period") + 天 (tiān, "day; sky") forms a term used for naming days of the week in modern Chinese. 星 (xīng, "star") originally refers to the stars in the sky and implies celestial patterns, while 期 (qī, "period") denotes a recurring interval or cycle. 天 (tiān, "day; sky") signifies a day within that cycle.
  - **interpretation:** 星 (xīng, "star") hints at a heavenly cycle like the repeating patterns of stars, combined with 期 (qī, "period") signifying a set timeframe. The phrase thus describes a cyclical series of days. 天 (tiān, "day") specifies the particular day in this sequence, here meaning 'a day within the cosmic week,' specifically 星期天, the day we call Sunday.
- **examples:**
  - 星期天我们(們)去公园(園)。
    - Xīngqītiān wǒmen qù gōngyuán.
    - On Sunday, we go to the park.
  - 这(這)个(個)星期天会(會)很热(熱)。
    - Zhège xīngqītiān huì hěn rè.
    - This Sunday will be very hot.
  - 星期天是我最喜欢(歡)的日子。
    - Xīngqītiān shì wǒ zuì xǐhuān de rìzi.
    - Sunday is my favorite day.
### 星期天 → 星
- **definition:** star
- **pinyin:** xīng
- **components:**
  - 晶
    - jīng
    - twinkling stars
  - 生
    - shēng
    - life; birth
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 晶 (jīng, 'twinkling stars') + phonetic 生 (shēng) ->
    - meaning
  - **interpretation:** The character originally depicted twinkling stars with 晶 (jīng, 'twinkling stars') indicating the twinkling or shining quality. The phonetic component 生 (shēng) was added to support the pronunciation but ultimately did not carry a separate semantic load. This compounded form solidified the modern representation of 'star'.
- **examples:**
  - 夜空中有许(許)多闪(閃)烁(爍)的星星。
    - Yèkōng zhōng yǒu xǔduō shǎnshuò de xīngxing.
    - There are many twinkling stars in the night sky.
  - 她的眼睛像星星一样(樣)明亮。
    - Tā de yǎnjing xiàng xīngxing yīyàng míngliàng.
    - Her eyes are as bright as stars.
  - 孩子们(們)在数(數)星星。
    - Háizimen zài shǔ xīngxing.
    - The children are counting stars.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 星](@media/glyph661f.png)
### 星期天 → 星 → 晶
- **definition:** twinkling stars
- **pinyin:** jīng
- **components:**
  - 日
    - rì
    - sun
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 日 (rì, "sun") x 3 =
    - multiple suns shining brightly ->
    - bright; sparkle; crystal
  - **interpretation:** The character 晶(jīng, "sparkle; crystal; bright") is formed by three 日 (rì, "sun") characters combined to visually represent multiple suns. This suggests an intense brilliance or sparkle, much like how multiple suns would create a radiant or crystal-like shine.
- **examples:**
  - 她的眼睛像晶石一样(樣)明亮。
    - Tā de yǎnjīng xiàng jīngshí yīyàng míngliàng.
    - Her eyes are as bright as crystals.
  - 窗户(戶)上结(結)了许(許)多冰晶。
    - Chuānghù shàng jié le xǔduō bīngjīng.
    - Many ice crystals have formed on the window.
  - 这(這)个(個)城市的夜景闪(閃)烁(爍)着(著)晶光。
    - Zhège chéngshì de yèjǐng shǎnshuò zhe jīngguāng.
    - The night view of the city sparkles brightly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 晶](@media/glyph6676.png)
### 星期天 → 星 → 晶 → 日
- **definition:** sun
- **pinyin:** rì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts the sun; a dot or line added in the center to distinguish from similar characters e.g. 囗
  - **interpretation:** As a pictogram, 日(rì, 'sun') directly represents the sun. In ancient times, the added dot helped visually differentiate it from other characters. This is analogous to the astronomical symbol ☉ and Egyptian hieroglyph 𓇳, both depicting the sun.
- **examples:**
  - 晨曦来(來)临(臨)时(時)，日出东(東)方。
    - Chénxī láilín shí, rìchū dōngfāng.
    - At the break of dawn, the sun rises in the east.
  - 温(溫)暖的日光洒(灑)满(滿)大地。
    - Wēnnuǎn de rìguāng sǎ mǎn dàdì.
    - The warm sunlight spreads over the earth.
  - 中午时(時)分，日高挂(掛)天。
    - Zhōngwǔ shífēn, rì gāo guà tiān.
    - At noon, the sun hangs high in the sky.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 日](@media/glyph65e5.png)
### 星期天 → 星 → 生
- **definition:** life; birth
- **pinyin:** shēng
- **components:**
  - 屮
    - chè
    - sprout
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 屮 (chè, "sprout") on top of a horizontal line ->
    - signifies a plant sprouting from the ground ->
    - symbolizes life
  - **interpretation:** The character 生 (shēng, "life") represents the concept of life force or vitality, symbolized by a sprout emerging from the earth, embodying growth and renewal.
- **examples:**
  - 生命是一场(場)美丽(麗)的旅程。
    - Shēngmìng shì yī chǎng měilì de lǚchéng.
    - Life is a beautiful journey.
  - 他在战(戰)场(場)上奋(奮)力生存。
    - Tā zài zhànchǎng shàng fènlì shēngcún.
    - He fights to live on the battlefield.
  - 这(這)家餐厅(廳)的生鱼(魚)片非常新鲜(鮮)。
    - Zhè jiā cāntīng de shēngyúpiàn fēicháng xīnxiān.
    - The raw fish slices at this restaurant are very fresh.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 生](@media/glyph751f.png)
### 星期天 → 星 → 生 → 屮
- **definition:** sprout
- **pinyin:** chè
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a sprout emerging from the ground
  - **interpretation:** 屮 (chè, 'sprout') is a pictogram that directly represents a young plant or sprout emerging from the ground. Its visual form captures the essence of new growth, and it historically served as an early representation of plant life or new vegetation.
- **examples:**
  - 春雨滋润(潤)后(後)，小屮冲(沖)破泥土而出。
    - chūn yǔ zī rùn hòu, xiǎo chè chōng pò ní tǔ ér chū.
    - After the spring rain nurtured the earth, the little sprout broke through the soil.
  - 草屮初生露尖端。
    - cǎo chè chū shēng lù jiān duān.
    - The grass sprout's tip has just emerged.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 屮](@media/glyph5c6e.png)
### 星期天 → 期
- **definition:** period; phase; time
- **pinyin:** qī
- **components:**
  - 其
    - qí
    - his
  - 月
    - yuè
    - moon
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 其 (qí) + semantic 月 (yuè, "moon") ->
    - changing moon marks passage of time ->
    - period of time
  - **interpretation:** The character 期(qī, "period") combines the phonetic 其 (qí, "his") with the semantic 月 (yuè, "moon") to signify the phases of the moon, which naturally represent cycles and periods of time. The moon's regular changes provide a clear, cyclical marker of time's passage.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)个(個)项(項)目需要完成的时(時)间(間)是三个(個)月。
    - Zhège xiàngmù xūyào wánchéng de shíjiān shì sān gè yuè.
    - The period required to complete this project is three months.
  - 在考试(試)期间(間)，请(請)保持安静(靜)。
    - Zài kǎoshì qījiān, qǐng bǎochí ānjìng.
    - During the exam period, please remain quiet.
  - 我们(們)在下一个(個)阶(階)段继(繼)续(續)努力。
    - Wǒmen zài xià yī gè jiēduàn jìxù nǔlì.
    - We will continue to work hard in the next phase.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 期](@media/glyph671f.png)
### 星期天 → 期 → 其
- **definition:** his
- **pinyin:** qí
- **components:**
  - 丌
    - qí
    - stand
  - 箕
    - jī
    - basket
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 𠀠 (basket) ->
    - 𠔝 with added 丌 (stand, phonetic) ->
    - borrowed as pronoun
  - **interpretation:** Originally depicted a basket (𠀠), which later included a stand (丌) beneath it to stabilize the image on bronze inscriptions, forming 𠔝. This combination was later borrowed for its sound to represent the pronoun 'his, her, its', and the basket meaning was reassigned to 箕 (jī, 'basket').
- **examples:**
  - 他把其思绪(緒)整理了一遍。
    - Tā bǎ qí sīxù zhěnglǐ le yī biàn.
    - He organized his thoughts once.
  - 其琴声(聲)如水般柔软(軟)。
    - Qí qín shēng rú shuǐ bān róuruǎn.
    - His playing is as soft as water.
  - 其计(計)划(劃)得到了同事们(們)的支持。
    - Qí jìhuà dédào le tóngshìmen de zhīchí.
    - His plan received the support of his colleagues.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 其](@media/glyph5176.png)
### 星期天 → 期 → 其 → 丌
- **definition:** stand
- **pinyin:** qí
- **components:**
  - 其
    - qí
    - his
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a support or stand for a basket ->
    - later representation of a table
  - **interpretation:** The character 丌 (jī, "table") originally represents a stand or support and was used as a component under 其 (qí, "his") to depict a basket on a stand. This association serves as its link to the meaning of 'table', conceptualizing a flat-topped support structure. This character was an ancient form of 其 and primarily served as a physical depiction of a supporting stand.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 丌](@media/glyph4e0c.png)
### 星期天 → 期 → 其 → 箕
- **definition:** basket
- **pinyin:** jī
- **components:**
  - 竹
    - zhú
    - bamboo
  - 其
    - qí
    - his
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 竹 (zhú, "bamboo") + phonetic 其 (qí, "his") ->
    - basket made of bamboo
  - **interpretation:** The character 箕(jī, "basket") combines 竹 (zhú, "bamboo") as the semantic component, indicating that the item is made of bamboo, with 其 (qí, "his") serving as the phonetic component to provide the sound. Originally, 其 (qí, "his") depicted a basket or container shape, and accordingly, 箕 specializes in the meaning related to a bamboo basket.
- **examples:**
  - 他用箕收集落下的叶(葉)子。
    - Tā yòng jī shōují luòxià de yèzi.
    - He uses a basket to collect fallen leaves.
  - 箕的大小非常适(適)合装(裝)米。
    - Jī de dàxiǎo fēicháng shìhé zhuāng mǐ.
    - The size of the basket is perfect for holding rice.
  - 那个(個)老人总(總)在集市上卖(賣)他编(編)的箕。
    - Nàge lǎorén zǒng zài jíshì shàng mài tā biān de jī.
    - That old man always sells the baskets he weaves at the market.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 箕](@media/glyph7b95.png)
### 星期天 → 期 → 其 → 箕 → 竹
- **definition:** bamboo
- **pinyin:** zhú
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts bamboo stalks with leaves
  - **interpretation:** The character 竹 (zhú, "bamboo") visually represents two stalks of bamboo with leaves at the top, illustrating the appearance of bamboo plants traditionally found in nature.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)根竹坚(堅)韧(韌)且美丽(麗)。
    - Zhè gēn zhú jiān rèn qiě měi lì.
    - This bamboo is strong and beautiful.
  - 竹子在风(風)中摇(搖)曳，发(發)出沙沙的声(聲)音。
    - Zhúzi zài fēng zhōng yáo yè, fā chū shā shā de shēng yīn.
    - The bamboo sways in the wind, making a rustling sound.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 竹](@media/glyph7af9.png)
### 星期天 → 期 → 月
- **definition:** moon
- **pinyin:** yuè
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a crescent moon
  - **interpretation:** The character 月(yuè, "moon") is a pictographic representation of a crescent moon, straightforwardly capturing the curved shape often associated with the moon's appearance. Though interchangeable with 夕 (xī, "evening") in the past, it distinctly represents the moon in this usage.
- **examples:**
  - 夜空挂(掛)着(著)明月。
    - Yè kōng guà zhe míng yuè.
    - The bright moon hangs in the night sky.
  - 人们(們)赏(賞)月，寄托(託)相思。
    - Rén men shǎng yuè, jì tuō xiāng sī.
    - People enjoy the moon, expressing their longing.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 月](@media/glyph6708.png)
### 星期天 → 天
- **definition:** day; sky
- **pinyin:** tiān
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Horizontal line above 大(dà, "big") to depict sky ->
    - anthropomorphic man with large head symbolizing heaven
  - **interpretation:** The character 天(tiān) originally depicts the sky as a horizontal line above a person with outstretched arms, 大(dà, "big"), emphasizing the vastness or domain of heaven. Over time, the character evolved into an anthropomorphic representation of heaven, which later influenced its interpretation in classical texts.
- **examples:**
  - 夜幕降临(臨)，天边(邊)星光闪(閃)烁(爍)。
    - Yèmù jiànglín, tiānbiān xīnguāng shǎnshuò.
    - As night falls, starlight gleams on the horizon.
  - 他仰望高空，祈求天佑众(眾)生。
    - Tā yǎngwàng gāokōng, qíqiú tiānyòu zhòngshēng.
    - He gazes up to the sky and prays for heaven's protection over all living beings.
- **historical forms:**

## 星期天
### xīngqītiān

## Sunday
%%%
## 从(從)到
---
## from … to …
### cóng … dào …
---
- **traditional:** 從到
- **definition:** from … to …
- **pinyin:** cóng … dào …
- **components:**
  - 從
    - cóng
    - follow; from
  - 到
    - dào
    - arrive; to
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 從 (cóng, "follow; from") combined with 到 (dào, "arrive; to") creates a phrase that indicates a span or movement from one point to another.
  - **interpretation:** 從 (cóng, "follow; from") indicates the starting point or origin of a movement or action. 到 (dào, "arrive; to") signifies the end or destination point. Together, this structure describes a range or transition, illustrating the path or timeline from one point (從) to another (到), effectively mapping out a continuous trajectory or sequence.
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)从(從)学(學)校到公园(園)。
    - Wǒmen cóng xuéxiào dào gōngyuán.
    - We go from the school to the park.
  - 从(從)春季到夏季，花儿(兒)都在盛开(開)。
    - Cóng chūnjì dào xiàjì, huā'ér dōu zài shèngkāi.
    - From spring to summer, flowers are in full bloom.
  - 他的工作时(時)间(間)是从(從)早上九点(點)到晚上五点(點)。
    - Tā de gōngzuò shíjiān shì cóng zǎoshang jiǔ diǎn dào wǎnshang wǔ diǎn.
    - His working hours are from 9 AM to 5 PM.
### 从(從)到 → 從
- **definition:** follow; from
- **pinyin:** cóng
- **components:**
  - 辵
    - chuò
    - walk; movement
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 辵 (chuò, "walk; movement") + phonetic 从(從) (cóng, "follow") ->
    - follow; from
  - **interpretation:** 從 (cóng, "follow") uses the movement component, 辵 (chuò, "walk"), to signify the concept of walking or following in a direction. Together with 从(從) as the phonetic element providing the sound, this combination effectively represents the idea of following someone or something on a path, hence the meanings 'follow' and 'from'.
  - **simplification:** This character retains its original traditional form from Chinese history, whereas its simplified counterpart 从 suggests a person walking with another person, highlighting a reduction of strokes for simplicity.
- **examples:**
  - 我从(從)家里(裡)出发(發)，去学(學)校。
    - Wǒ cóng jiā lǐ chūfā, qù xuéxiào.
    - I set off from home to go to school.
  - 他从(從)不迟(遲)到，总(總)是准(準)时(時)来(來)。
    - Tā cóng bù chídào, zǒng shì zhǔnshí lái.
    - He is never late and always arrives on time.
  - 从(從)今天开(開)始，我要努力学(學)习(習)。
    - Cóng jīntiān kāishǐ, wǒ yào nǔlì xuéxí.
    - Starting from today, I will study hard.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 從](@media/glyph5f9e.png)
### 从(從)到 → 從 → 辵
- **definition:** walk; movement
- **pinyin:** chuò
- **components:**
  - 彳
    - chì
    - walk
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - foot
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 彳 (chì, "walk") + 止 (zhǐ, "foot" or "to stop") ->
    - 𣥆 ->
    - stylized as 龰 ->
    - 辵
  - **interpretation:** The character 辵 combines 彳 (chì, "walk"), which represents movement, with 止 (zhǐ, "foot" or "to stop"), suggesting the concept of stepping or traveling forward. This character represents the idea of movement, particularly the action of walking or traveling, as originally depicted by the more conservative form 𣥆. Over time, the bottom component has been stylized as 龰, forming the current representation.
- **examples:**
  - 他辵在乡(鄉)间(間)的小路上。
    - Tā chuò zài xiāngjiān de xiǎolù shàng.
    - He walks on the rural path.
  - 晨光洒(灑)满(滿)大地，他辵出门(門)开(開)始旅程。
    - Chén guāng sǎ mǎn dàdì, tā chuò chūmén kāishǐ lǚchéng.
    - As the morning light fills the earth, he sets out to begin his journey.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 辵](@media/glyph8fb5.png)
### 从(從)到 → 從 → 辵 → 彳
- **definition:** walk
- **pinyin:** chì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a foot or person walking
  - **interpretation:** 彳(chì, 'walking') visually represents steps or a person moving, suggesting the idea of walking or movement. Despite a simplified history from characters like 行(xíng, 'walk'), its pictographic heritage directly connects with the notion of stepping or proceeding.
- **examples:**
  - 他喜欢(歡)在河边(邊)慢慢地走。
    - Tā xǐhuān zài hé biān mànmàn de zǒu.
    - He likes to walk slowly by the river.
  - 我们(們)每天退出喧嚣(囂)，享受安静(靜)的散步。
    - Wǒmen měitiān tuìchū xuānxiāo, xiǎngshòu ānjìng de sànbù.
    - We withdraw from the hustle and bustle every day to enjoy a quiet walk.
  - 他常常独(獨)自彳亍于(於)公园(園)小径(徑)。
    - Tā chángcháng dúzì chìchù yú gōngyuán xiǎojìng.
    - He often walks alone on the park trails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 彳](@media/glyph5f73.png)
### 从(從)到 → 從 → 辵 → 止
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 趾
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 龰
    - yù
    - stylized feet
  - 手
    - shǒu
    - hand
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Original: Foot pointing up with 3 toes and a sole ->
    - Stylized as 龰 ->
    - Derivative 趾 refers to original 'foot' meaning
  - **interpretation:** Originally depicting a footprint with toes and a sole, 止 (zhǐ, "foot") represents the foot. The character's form resembles a foot with three toes, analogous to how the hand is represented with fingers in other characters.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)的止需要静(靜)养(養)。
    - Tā shòu shāng de zhǐ xū yào jìng yǎng.
    - His injured foot needs adequate rest.
  - 他走路时(時)小心谨(謹)慎，因为(爲)止若受伤(傷)便难(難)前行。
    - Tā zǒu lù shí xiǎo xīn jǐn shèn, yīn wèi zhǐ ruò shòu shāng biàn nán qián xíng.
    - He walks carefully because if his foot gets injured, it becomes difficult to move forward.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 止](@media/glyph6b62.png)
### 从(從)到 → 從 → 辵 → 止 → 趾
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 足
    - zú
    - foot
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - halt
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 足 (zú, "foot") + phonetic 止 (zhǐ) ->
    - toe
  - **interpretation:** The character combines 足 (zú, "foot"), indicating the general area involved, with 止 (zhǐ) providing the sound and potentially suggesting the idea of a part of the foot that 'halts' or 'stops' progression, which naturally leads to the notion of a toe.
- **examples:**
  - 他的脚(腳)趾受伤(傷)了。
    - Tā de jiǎozhǐ shòushāng le.
    - His toe is injured.
  - 她用脚(腳)趾轻(輕)轻(輕)地踢了一下球。
    - Tā yòng jiǎozhǐ qīngqīng de tī le yīxià qiú.
    - She gently kicked the ball with her toe.
  - 在沙滩(灘)上散步时(時)，我感受到沙子在我的脚(腳)趾间(間)流动(動)。
    - Zài shātān shàng sànbù shí, wǒ gǎnshòu dào shāzi zài wǒ de jiǎozhǐ jiān liúdòng.
    - While walking on the beach, I felt the sand flowing between my toes.
### 从(從)到 → 從 → 辵 → 止 → 趾 → 足
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zú
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a leg ->
    - originally depicted as ⽦ ->
    - represents 'foot'
  - **interpretation:** The character 足(zú, 'foot') is a pictographic representation of a human leg, which directly portrays the concept of a 'foot'. The pictographic origin emphasizes its fundamental meaning in the language.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)后(後)，他的足不能动(動)。
    - tā shòushāng hòu, tā de zú bù néng dòng。
    - After he was injured, his foot couldn't move.
  - 小明打球时(時)，不小心扭伤(傷)了足。
    - xiǎo míng dǎ qiú shí, bù xiǎoxīn niǔ shāng le zú。
    - When Xiaoming was playing ball, he accidentally twisted his foot.
  - 我每天锻(鍛)炼(鍊)足部。
    - wǒ měitiān duànliàn zúbù。
    - I exercise my foot muscles every day.
- **historical forms:**

### 从(從)到 → 從 → 辵 → 止 → 龰
- **definition:** stylized feet
- **pinyin:** yù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a stylized footprint pointing upward ->
    - originally meaning 'foot' ->
    - later forms like 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') refer back to original meaning
  - **interpretation:** 龰 (yù, 'stylized feet') is a pictogram showing a footprint pointing up, originally indicating the concept of a foot. The character 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') evolved from this and retains the reference to the original meaning. It visually resembles a sole with three toes, similar to representations of the human hand in characters like 爪 (zhuǎ, 'claw'), 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), and 又 (yòu, 'again').
### 从(從)到 → 從 → 辵 → 止 → 手
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** shǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a hand with fingers; top stroke is a bent over middle finger, horizontal strokes represent fingers
  - **interpretation:** The character 手 (shǒu, "hand") is a direct pictorial representation of a human hand with all five fingers, which distinguishes it from similar characters representing claws or simplified fingers. This visually conveys its meaning as a hand clearly.
- **examples:**
  - 他用手写(寫)字。
    - Tā yòng shǒu xiě zì.
    - He writes with his hand.
  - 妈(媽)妈(媽)牵(牽)着(著)我的手走路。
    - Māmā qiān zhe wǒ de shǒu zǒu lù.
    - Mom holds my hand while walking.
  - 他的手很温(溫)暖，带(帶)给(給)我力量。
    - Tā de shǒu hěn wēn nuǎn, dài gěi wǒ lìliàng.
    - His hand is very warm, giving me strength.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 手](@media/glyph624b.png)
### 从(從)到 → 到
- **definition:** arrive; to
- **pinyin:** dào
- **components:**
  - 至
    - zhì
    - to arrive
  - 刀
    - dāo
    - knife
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 至 (zhì, "to arrive") + phonetic 刀 (dāo) ->
    - to arrive, reach
  - **interpretation:** The character 到(dào, "to") combines the meaning of 至 (zhì, "to arrive"), indicating movement or arrival at a destination, with the phonetic component 刀 (dāo) to provide the pronunciation. This construction intuitively conveys the action of reaching a point or destination.
- **examples:**
  - 我刚(剛)到学(學)校。
    - Wǒ gāng dào xuéxiào.
    - I just arrived at school.
  - 他从(從)北京到上海。
    - Tā cóng Běijīng dào Shànghǎi.
    - He went from Beijing to Shanghai.
  - 我们(們)到那里(裡)时(時)，天已经(經)黑了。
    - Wǒmen dào nàlǐ shí, tiān yǐjīng hēi le.
    - By the time we got there, it was already dark.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 到](@media/glyph5230.png)
### 从(從)到 → 到 → 至
- **definition:** to arrive
- **pinyin:** zhì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** Ideogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts an arrow stuck into the ground ->
    - express arrival or reaching a destination
  - **interpretation:** The image of an arrow embedded in the ground symbolizes reaching a fixed endpoint, evoking the idea of arriving at a particular place.
- **examples:**
  - 火车(車)已至。
    - Huǒchē yǐ zhì.
    - The train has arrived.
  - 从(從)广(廣)州出发(發)，火车(車)已至目的地。
    - Cóng Guǎngzhōu chūfā, huǒchē yǐ zhì mùdìdì.
    - Departing from Guangzhou, the train has arrived at its destination.
  - 信使至长(長)安。
    - Xìnshǐ zhì Cháng'ān.
    - The messenger has arrived in Chang'an.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 至](@media/glyph81f3.png)
### 从(從)到 → 到 → 刀
- **definition:** knife
- **pinyin:** dāo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a knife
  - **interpretation:** 刀 (dāo, "knife") is a pictographic representation of a knife or blade, with a sharp edge and a handle, resembling the form of a basic cutting tool.
- **examples:**
  - 他用锋(鋒)利的刀，切开(開)蔬菜。
    - tā yòng fēnglì de dāo, qiē kāi shūcài.
    - He uses a sharp knife to cut vegetables.
  - 这(這)把刀非常锋(鋒)利。
    - zhè bǎ dāo fēicháng fēnglì.
    - This knife is very sharp.
  - 厨(廚)师(師)小心地持刀，为(為)客人切肉。
    - chúshī xiǎoxīn de chí dāo, wèi kèrén qiē ròu.
    - The chef holds the knife carefully and slices meat for the guest.

## 房子
---
## house
### fángzi
---
- **definition:** house
- **pinyin:** fángzi
- **components:**
  - 房
    - fáng
    - house; building
  - 子
    - zi
    - child; small thing; noun suffix
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 房 (fáng, "house") refers to a building or structure for dwelling; 子 (zi, "child; small thing") often indicates a diminutive or noun suffix, implying a specific type or instance.
  - **interpretation:** 房 (fáng, "house") conveys the primary concept of a building or space for living. 子 (zi, "child; small thing") functions as a nominalizing suffix, turning the general idea into a concrete, specific term for 'a house' or 'home'. The use of 子 suggests intimacy or familiarity, as if referring to a 'little home' or a place of belonging.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)座房子很漂亮。
    - Zhè zuò fángzi hěn piàoliang.
    - This house is very beautiful.
  - 村里(裡)的人正在建造一座新房子。
    - Cūn lǐ de rén zhèngzài jiànzào yī zuò xīn fángzi.
    - The villagers are building a new house.
  - 他们(們)打算卖(賣)掉老房子，然后(後)搬到城市。
    - Tāmen dǎsuàn mài diào lǎo fángzi, ránhòu bān dào chéngshì.
    - They plan to sell the old house and then move to the city.
### 房子 → 房
- **definition:** house; building
- **pinyin:** fáng
- **components:**
  - 戶
    - hù
    - door
  - 方
    - fāng
    - side
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - 戶 (hù, "door") + 方 (fāng, "side") =
    - door on the side ->
    - room
  - **interpretation:** 房(fáng, "house; room") combines the semantic element 戶 (hù, "door") with the phonetic element 方 (fāng, "side"), suggesting a space associated with a door, like a side room in a house.
- **examples:**
  - 他在城里(裡)租了一间(間)房。
    - Tā zài chénglǐ zū le yī jiān fáng.
    - He rented a room in the city.
  - 我的房子很温(溫)暖。
    - Wǒ de fángzi hěn wēnnuǎn.
    - My house is very warm.
  - 夏天时(時)房间(間)有空调(調)，感觉(覺)十分舒适(適)。
    - Xiàtiān shí fángjiān yǒu kōngtiáo, gǎnjué shífēn shūshì.
    - In summer, the room has air conditioning and feels very comfortable.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 房](@media/glyph623f.png)
### 房子 → 房 → 戶
- **definition:** door
- **pinyin:** hù
- **components:**
  - 門
    - mén
    - gate
  - 𠁣
    - unknown
    - unknown
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts one-half of 門 (mén, "gate") ->
    - stylized as 𠁣 ->
    - final form 戶 (hù, "door")
  - **interpretation:** The character 戶 (hù, "door") represents a single door panel, derived from the depiction of half a gate, symbolizing entry or a threshold.
  - **simplification:** 户 is a simplified and variant traditional form of 戶, streamlining the pictorial elements to a more abstract representation, but retaining the symbolic essence of a door or entrance.
- **examples:**
  - 他推开(開)了戶。
    - Tā tuī kāi le hù.
    - He pushed open the door.
  - 夜晚降临(臨)时(時)，古宅的戶缓(緩)缓(緩)开(開)启(啟)。
    - Yè wǎn jiàng lín shí, gǔ zhái de hù huǎn huǎn kāi qǐ.
    - When night falls, the door of the ancient house slowly opens.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 戶](@media/glyph6236.png)
### 房子 → 房 → 戶 → 門
- **definition:** gate
- **pinyin:** mén
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a double-door gate
  - **interpretation:** The character depicts a pair of doors, visually representing the concept of a door or gate, which is fundamental in indicating entrance and exit points in structures.
- **examples:**
  - 我走到门(門)口。
    - Wǒ zǒu dào ménkǒu.
    - I walk to the door.
  - 门(門)轻(輕)轻(輕)打开(開)，房客进(進)来(來)了。
    - Mén qīngqīng dǎkāi, fángkè jìn láile.
    - The door opened gently, and the tenant came in.
- **historical forms:**

### 房子 → 房 → 戶 → 𠁣
- **definition:** unknown
- **pinyin:** unknown
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a hand holding a tool
  - **interpretation:** This character appears to represent a hand holding an object, possibly related to actions involving grasping or manipulation. It is not commonly used in modern Chinese, but may appear in specialized contexts or as an ancient form.
### 房子 → 房 → 方
- **definition:** side
- **pinyin:** fāng
- **components:**
  - 一
    - yī
    - one
  - 刀
    - dāo
    - sword
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 一 (yī, "one") + 刀 (dāo, "sword") =
    - original depiction of blade's tip ->
    - borrowed for "side" ->
    - now "square"
  - **interpretation:** Initially depicting the blade of a sword, 方 (fāng, "square") was later borrowed for its current meaning due to its association with edges and boundaries, metaphorically expanded to define sides and squares.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)张(張)桌子是方的。
    - Zhè zhāng zhuōzi shì fāng de.
    - This table is square.
  - 院子里(裡)铺(鋪)满(滿)了方砖(磚)。
    - Yuànzi lǐ pū mǎn le fāng zhuān.
    - The courtyard is paved with square bricks.
  - 我买(買)的花瓶是方形的，设(設)计(計)简(簡)洁(潔)优(優)美。
    - Wǒ mǎi de huāpíng shì fāngxíng de, shèjì jiǎnjié yōuměi.
    - The vase I bought is square, with a simple and elegant design.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 方](@media/glyph65b9.png)
### 房子 → 房 → 方 → 一
- **definition:** one
- **pinyin:** yī
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:** A horizontal stroke representing the concept of 'one'.
  - **interpretation:** The character 一(yī, "one") is a simple horizontal line signifying the singular and unified concept of 'one'. It directly represents being singular or the number one.
- **examples:**
  - 我有一个(個)苹(蘋)果。
    - Wǒ yǒu yī gè píngguǒ.
    - I have one apple.
  - 他只看到一只(隻)鸟(鳥)，飞(飛)进(進)了花园(園)。
    - Tā zhǐ kàn dào yī zhī niǎo, fēi jìn le huā yuán.
    - He only saw one bird, which flew into the garden.
  - 一条(條)直路通向远(遠)方。
    - Yī tiáo zhí lù tōng xiàng yuǎn fāng.
    - One straight road leads to the distance.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 一](@media/glyph4e00.png)

- **pinyin:** dāo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a knife
  - **interpretation:** 刀 (dāo, "knife") is a pictographic representation of a knife or blade, with a sharp edge and a handle, resembling the form of a basic cutting tool.

### 房子 → 子

- **pinyin:** zi
- **etymology:**

  - **description:** Depicts a baby with a large head and spread arms, with legs wrapped in a blanket
  - **interpretation:** The character 子(zǐ, "child") is a pictorial representation of a baby, emphasizing characteristics like a large head and outstretched arms typical of infants, which conveys the essence of a child. This visual element helps infer its meaning.

  - 这(這)小子很调(調)皮。

## 第一次
---
## first time
### dì yī cì
---
- **definition:** first time
- **pinyin:** dì yī cì
- **components:**
  - 第
    - dì
    - prefix for ordinal numbers
  - 一
    - yī
    - one
  - 次
    - cì
    - time; occurrence
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 第 (dì, "prefix for ordinal numbers") is a prefix used to indicate the order or rank in a sequence, such as 'first', 'second', etc. 一 (yī, "one") specifies the number 'one'. 次 (cì, "time; occurrence") refers to an instance or occurrence of an event. Combined, 第 (dì, "prefix for ordinal numbers") + 一 (yī, "one") + 次 (cì, "time; occurrence") literally translates to the 'first instance' or 'first occurrence', thus meaning 'first time'.
  - **interpretation:** 第 (dì, "prefix for ordinal numbers") provides the ordinal sense, indicating position or sequence in a list. Following it, 一 (yī, "one") specifies the position as 'first', establishing the sequence. 次 (cì, "time; occurrence") then gives the notion of an event or instance. This leads to the understanding of 第一次 as 'the first event in a sequence' or simply 'the first time'.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)是我第一次去北京。
    - Zhè shì wǒ dì yī cì qù Běijīng.
    - This is my first time going to Beijing.
  - 他第一次看到大海，感到非常兴(興)奋(奮)。
    - Tā dì yī cì kàn dào dàhǎi, gǎndào fēicháng xīngfèn.
    - He felt very excited when he saw the sea for the first time.
  - 我们(們)第一次见(見)面，是在一个(個)朋友的聚会(會)。
    - Wǒmen dì yī cì jiànmiàn, shì zài yī gè péngyǒu de jùhuì.
    - The first time we met was at a friend's party.
### 第一次 → 第
- **definition:** prefix for ordinal numbers
- **pinyin:** dì
- **components:**
  - 𥫗
    - zhú
    - bamboo
  - 弟
    - dì
    - younger brother
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - 𥫗 (zhú, "bamboo") + 弟 (dì) =
    - bamboo strips used for writing ->
    - order/sequencing concept
  - **interpretation:** The character 第(dì) combines the semantic element 𥫗 (zhú, "bamboo") with the phonetic element 弟 (dì). Bamboo was historically used for writing documents, such as lists or sequences, which informs the idea of ordering denoted by 第(dì).
- **examples:**
  - 我在第二医(醫)院工作，每天接待第一批病人。
    - Wǒ zài dì èr yīyuàn gōngzuò, měitiān jiēdài dì yī pī bìngrén.
    - I work at the Second Hospital and every day I receive the first group of patients.
  - 今天老师(師)讲(講)解第二十五课(課)，布(佈)置第十二个(個)作业(業)。
    - Jīntiān lǎoshī jiǎngjiě dì èr shí wǔ kè, bùzhì dì shí èr gè zuòyè.
    - Today the teacher explained the 25th lesson and assigned the 12th homework.
  - 比赛(賽)中，他拿到第一名。
    - Bǐsài zhōng, tā ná dào dì yī míng.
    - During the competition, he won first place.
### 第一次 → 第 → 𥫗
- **definition:** bamboo
- **pinyin:** zhú
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts two bamboo stalks with leaves ->
    - earlier forms resembled 个 + 个 ->
    - current form resembles ケ + ケ or 亇 + 亇
  - **interpretation:** The character 𥫗 visually represents two bamboo stalks with leaves, capturing the botanical appearance of bamboo. Earlier iterations of the character resembled 个 + 个, indicating the dual stalks, while the current form stylizes this into ケ + ケ or 亇 + 亇, emphasizing the leaf and stalk structure.
- **examples:**
  - 青翠的𥫗点(點)缀(綴)在山坡上。
    - Qīngcuì de zhú diǎn zhuì zài shānpō shàng.
    - The verdant bamboo decorates the hillside.
  - 小河边(邊)的古亭旁有一丛(叢)𥫗，风(風)中它轻(輕)轻(輕)摇(搖)曳。
    - Xiǎo hé biān de gǔ tíng páng yǒu yī cóng zhú, fēng zhōng tā qīngqīng yáoyè.
    - By the small river next to the ancient pavilion, a clump of bamboo gently sways in the wind.
### 第一次 → 第 → 弟
- **definition:** younger brother
- **pinyin:** dì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a spear handle wrapped in a leather strap ->
    - signifies order/sequence ->
    - extended meaning to 'younger brother'
  - **interpretation:** The character originally depicted a spear or handle with an ordered wrapping, symbolizing sequence or hierarchy, which logically extends to reference a younger brother in a family structure.
- **examples:**
  - 我最喜欢(歡)跟弟一起玩。
    - Wǒ zuì xǐhuān gēn dì yīqǐ wán.
    - I most enjoy playing with my younger brother.
  - 今天我带(帶)弟去公园(園)，一起放风(風)筝(箏)。
    - Jīntiān wǒ dài dì qù gōngyuán, yīqǐ fàng fēngzheng.
    - Today, I take my younger brother to the park to fly kites together.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 弟](@media/glyph5f1f.png)
### 第一次 → 一
- **definition:** one
- **pinyin:** yī
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:** A horizontal stroke representing the concept of 'one'.
  - **interpretation:** The character 一(yī, "one") is a simple horizontal line signifying the singular and unified concept of 'one'. It directly represents being singular or the number one.
- **examples:**
  - 我有一个(個)苹(蘋)果。
    - Wǒ yǒu yī gè píngguǒ.
    - I have one apple.
  - 他只看到一只(隻)鸟(鳥)，飞(飛)进(進)了花园(園)。
    - Tā zhǐ kàn dào yī zhī niǎo, fēi jìn le huā yuán.
    - He only saw one bird, which flew into the garden.
  - 一条(條)直路通向远(遠)方。
    - Yī tiáo zhí lù tōng xiàng yuǎn fāng.
    - One straight road leads to the distance.

### 第一次 → 次
- **definition:** time; occurrence
- **pinyin:** cì
- **components:**
  - 咨
    - zī
    - to sigh
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a person exhaling ->
    - Possibly original form of 咨 (zī, "to sigh")
  - **interpretation:** 次 (cì, "time; instance") originally depicted a person exhaling, indicative of a sigh or breath, which aligns with its original use related to respiration. Over time, it became abstracted to mean 'time' or 'instance' likely due to repetitive or rhythmic nature of breathing.
- **examples:**
  - 我去过(過)北京很多次。
    - Wǒ qù guò Běijīng hěn duō cì.
    - I have been to Beijing many times.
  - 经(經)过(過)第一次失败(敗)后(後)，他总(總)结(結)经(經)验(驗)。
    - Jīngguò dì yī cì shībài hòu, tā zǒngjié jīngyàn.
    - After failing the first time, he summed up his experience.
  - 这(這)次活动(動)充满(滿)乐(樂)趣。
    - Zhè cì huódòng chōngmǎn lèqù.
    - This event is full of fun.

### 第一次 → 次 → 咨
- **definition:** to sigh
- **pinyin:** zī
- **components:**
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
  - 次
    - cì
    - next; sequence
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 口 (kǒu, "mouth") + phonetic 次 (cì) ->
    - to sigh
  - **interpretation:** The component 口 (kǒu, "mouth") suggests the action of speaking or uttering a sound, while 次 (cì) provides the phonetic cue. The combination creates an image of expressing a sound or sigh through the mouth.
- **examples:**
  - 她轻(輕)轻(輕)地咨叹(嘆)了一声(聲)。
    - Tā qīngqīng de zī tàn le yī shēng.
    - She sighed softly.
  - 想到这(這)里(裡)，他忍不住咨了口气(氣)。
    - Xiǎngdào zhèlǐ, tā rěn bú zhù zīle kǒu qì.
    - Thinking of this, he couldn't help but sigh.
  - 每当(當)烦(煩)恼(惱)袭(襲)来(來)，我总(總)是咨一声(聲)。
    - Měi dāng fánnǎo xílái, wǒ zǒng shì zī yī shēng.
    - Whenever worries arise, I always let out a sigh.

### 第一次 → 次 → 咨 → 口
- **definition:** mouth
- **pinyin:** kǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth.
  - **interpretation:** The character 口(kǒu, 'mouth') is a straightforward pictogram that visually represents an open mouth. It is a fundamental character in the Chinese language, often used both as an independent word and as a component in more complex characters, lending a semantic association to ideas relating to speech, openings, or enclosures.
- **examples:**
  - 他张(張)开(開)口，大声(聲)喊叫。
    - Tā zhāngkāi kǒu, dàshēng hǎnjiào.
    - He opened his mouth and shouted loudly.
  - 这(這)口饭(飯)入口即化。
    - Zhè kǒu fàn rùkǒu jíhuà.
    - This mouthful of food melts in your mouth.
  - 小女孩咬了一口苹(蘋)果，露出甜美的笑容。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái yǎole yī kǒu píngguǒ, lùchū tiánměi de xiàoróng.
    - The little girl took a bite of the apple and smiled sweetly.

## 过(過)
---
## experiential aspect marker
### guò
---
- **traditional:** 過
- **definition:** experiential aspect marker
- **pinyin:** guò
- **components:**
  - 辵
    - chuò
    - walk; movement
  - 咼
    - guō
    - to exceed; to surpass
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 辵 (chuò, "walk; movement") + phonetic 咼 (guō) ->
    - exceed; pass through
  - **interpretation:** This character combines the semantic element 辵 (chuò, "walk; movement"), indicating movement or transit, with the phonetic element 咼 (guō), which suggests the sound. The concept of movement suggests the idea of passing or exceeding a certain point.
  - **simplification:** 过 is simplified by replacing 辵 (chuò, "walk; movement") with 辶, a simplified version of the radical indicating movement.
- **examples:**
  - 我已经(經)吃过(過)晚饭(飯)。
    - Wǒ yǐjīng chī guò wǎnfàn.
    - I have already had dinner.
  - 我们(們)经(經)过(過)美丽(麗)的公园(園)，继(繼)续(續)向前走。
    - Wǒmen jīngguò měilì de gōngyuán, jìxù xiàng qián zǒu.
    - We passed through the beautiful park and continued walking forward.
  - 他的成绩(績)超过(過)了所有同学(學)。
    - Tā de chéngjì chāoguòle suǒyǒu tóngxué.
    - His grades exceeded all his classmates.
### 过(過) → 辵
- **definition:** walk; movement
- **pinyin:** chuò
- **components:**
  - 彳
    - chì
    - walk
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - foot
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 彳 (chì, "walk") + 止 (zhǐ, "foot" or "to stop") ->
    - 𣥆 ->
    - stylized as 龰 ->
    - 辵
  - **interpretation:** The character 辵 combines 彳 (chì, "walk"), which represents movement, with 止 (zhǐ, "foot" or "to stop"), suggesting the concept of stepping or traveling forward. This character represents the idea of movement, particularly the action of walking or traveling, as originally depicted by the more conservative form 𣥆. Over time, the bottom component has been stylized as 龰, forming the current representation.
- **examples:**
  - 他辵在乡(鄉)间(間)的小路上。
    - Tā chuò zài xiāngjiān de xiǎolù shàng.
    - He walks on the rural path.
  - 晨光洒(灑)满(滿)大地，他辵出门(門)开(開)始旅程。
    - Chén guāng sǎ mǎn dàdì, tā chuò chūmén kāishǐ lǚchéng.
    - As the morning light fills the earth, he sets out to begin his journey.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 辵](@media/glyph8fb5.png)
### 过(過) → 辵 → 彳
- **definition:** walk
- **pinyin:** chì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a foot or person walking
  - **interpretation:** 彳(chì, 'walking') visually represents steps or a person moving, suggesting the idea of walking or movement. Despite a simplified history from characters like 行(xíng, 'walk'), its pictographic heritage directly connects with the notion of stepping or proceeding.
- **examples:**
  - 他喜欢(歡)在河边(邊)慢慢地走。
    - Tā xǐhuān zài hé biān mànmàn de zǒu.
    - He likes to walk slowly by the river.
  - 我们(們)每天退出喧嚣(囂)，享受安静(靜)的散步。
    - Wǒmen měitiān tuìchū xuānxiāo, xiǎngshòu ānjìng de sànbù.
    - We withdraw from the hustle and bustle every day to enjoy a quiet walk.
  - 他常常独(獨)自彳亍于(於)公园(園)小径(徑)。
    - Tā chángcháng dúzì chìchù yú gōngyuán xiǎojìng.
    - He often walks alone on the park trails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 彳](@media/glyph5f73.png)
### 过(過) → 辵 → 止
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 趾
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 龰
    - yù
    - stylized feet
  - 手
    - shǒu
    - hand
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Original: Foot pointing up with 3 toes and a sole ->
    - Stylized as 龰 ->
    - Derivative 趾 refers to original 'foot' meaning
  - **interpretation:** Originally depicting a footprint with toes and a sole, 止 (zhǐ, "foot") represents the foot. The character's form resembles a foot with three toes, analogous to how the hand is represented with fingers in other characters.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)的止需要静(靜)养(養)。
    - Tā shòu shāng de zhǐ xū yào jìng yǎng.
    - His injured foot needs adequate rest.
  - 他走路时(時)小心谨(謹)慎，因为(爲)止若受伤(傷)便难(難)前行。
    - Tā zǒu lù shí xiǎo xīn jǐn shèn, yīn wèi zhǐ ruò shòu shāng biàn nán qián xíng.
    - He walks carefully because if his foot gets injured, it becomes difficult to move forward.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 止](@media/glyph6b62.png)
### 过(過) → 辵 → 止 → 趾
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 足
    - zú
    - foot
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - halt
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 足 (zú, "foot") + phonetic 止 (zhǐ) ->
    - toe
  - **interpretation:** The character combines 足 (zú, "foot"), indicating the general area involved, with 止 (zhǐ) providing the sound and potentially suggesting the idea of a part of the foot that 'halts' or 'stops' progression, which naturally leads to the notion of a toe.
- **examples:**
  - 他的脚(腳)趾受伤(傷)了。
    - Tā de jiǎozhǐ shòushāng le.
    - His toe is injured.
  - 她用脚(腳)趾轻(輕)轻(輕)地踢了一下球。
    - Tā yòng jiǎozhǐ qīngqīng de tī le yīxià qiú.
    - She gently kicked the ball with her toe.
  - 在沙滩(灘)上散步时(時)，我感受到沙子在我的脚(腳)趾间(間)流动(動)。
    - Zài shātān shàng sànbù shí, wǒ gǎnshòu dào shāzi zài wǒ de jiǎozhǐ jiān liúdòng.
    - While walking on the beach, I felt the sand flowing between my toes.
### 过(過) → 辵 → 止 → 趾 → 足
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zú
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a leg ->
    - originally depicted as ⽦ ->
    - represents 'foot'
  - **interpretation:** The character 足(zú, 'foot') is a pictographic representation of a human leg, which directly portrays the concept of a 'foot'. The pictographic origin emphasizes its fundamental meaning in the language.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)后(後)，他的足不能动(動)。
    - tā shòushāng hòu, tā de zú bù néng dòng。
    - After he was injured, his foot couldn't move.
  - 小明打球时(時)，不小心扭伤(傷)了足。
    - xiǎo míng dǎ qiú shí, bù xiǎoxīn niǔ shāng le zú。
    - When Xiaoming was playing ball, he accidentally twisted his foot.
  - 我每天锻(鍛)炼(鍊)足部。
    - wǒ měitiān duànliàn zúbù。
    - I exercise my foot muscles every day.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 足](@media/glyph8db3.png)
### 过(過) → 辵 → 止 → 龰
- **definition:** stylized feet
- **pinyin:** yù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a stylized footprint pointing upward ->
    - originally meaning 'foot' ->
    - later forms like 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') refer back to original meaning
  - **interpretation:** 龰 (yù, 'stylized feet') is a pictogram showing a footprint pointing up, originally indicating the concept of a foot. The character 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') evolved from this and retains the reference to the original meaning. It visually resembles a sole with three toes, similar to representations of the human hand in characters like 爪 (zhuǎ, 'claw'), 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), and 又 (yòu, 'again').
### 过(過) → 辵 → 止 → 手
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** shǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a hand with fingers; top stroke is a bent over middle finger, horizontal strokes represent fingers
  - **interpretation:** The character 手 (shǒu, "hand") is a direct pictorial representation of a human hand with all five fingers, which distinguishes it from similar characters representing claws or simplified fingers. This visually conveys its meaning as a hand clearly.
- **examples:**
  - 他用手写(寫)字。
    - Tā yòng shǒu xiě zì.
    - He writes with his hand.
  - 妈(媽)妈(媽)牵(牽)着(著)我的手走路。
    - Māmā qiān zhe wǒ de shǒu zǒu lù.
    - Mom holds my hand while walking.
  - 他的手很温(溫)暖，带(帶)给(給)我力量。
    - Tā de shǒu hěn wēn nuǎn, dài gěi wǒ lìliàng.
    - His hand is very warm, giving me strength.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 手](@media/glyph624b.png)
### 过(過) → 咼
- **definition:** to exceed; to surpass
- **pinyin:** guō
- **components:**
  - 冎
    - guā
    - a type of ancient vessel
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 冎 (guā, "a type of ancient vessel") + semantic 口 (kǒu, "mouth") ->
    - crooked; bent
  - **interpretation:** The character 咼 (guō, "crooked, bent") combines the phonetic component 冎 (guā, "a type of ancient vessel"), which suggests the sound, with the semantic component 口 (kǒu, "mouth"), indicating aspects related to opening or shape. Together, these components infer an image of something that does not maintain a straight line, thus producing the meaning "crooked, bent."
- **historical forms:**
